حَتَّى بَدَتْ لَهُمْ شُمُوسُ الْمَعْرِفَهُ رَأَوْا مُخَدَّرَاتِهَا مُنْكَشِفَهُ
ثُمَّ إِنَّ المُخَدَّرَاتِ جَمْعُ: «مُخَدَّرَةِ»، وَهِيَ : المَرْأَةُ المُسْتَتِرَةُ تَحْتَ الخِدْرِ، لَكِنَّ المُرَادَ : مِنَ المُخَدَّرَاتِ هُنَا : المَسَائِلُ الخَفِيَّةُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الاسْتِعَارَةِ التَّصْرِيحِيَّةِ التَّبَعِيَّةِ، وَذَلِكَ بِأَنْ يُشَبَّهَ الخَفَاءُ بِمَعْنَى التَّحْدِيرِ ؛ بِجَامِعِ : عَدَمِ الظُّهُورِ فِي كُلِّ، وَيُسْتَعَارُ لَفْظُ المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ لِلمُشَبَّهِ، ثُمَّ يُشْتَقُ مِنْهُ «مُخَدَّرَاتٍ بِمَعْنَى : خَفِيَّاتٍ، وَالقَرِينَةُ : الإِضَافَةُ إِلَى الضَّمِيرِ العَائِدِ إِلَى المَعْرِفَةِ أَوِ السُّمُوسِ عَلَى مَا عَلِمْتَ، وَالرُّؤْيَةُ : تَرْشِيحٌ، وَكَذَا الإِنْكِشَافُ إِنْ كَانَ حَقِيقَةٌ فِي الحِرِّيَّاتِ فَقَطْ . وَمَا تَقَرَّرَ مِنْ أَنَّ الاِسْتِعَارَةَ تَبَعِيَّةٌ هُوَ المُوَافِقُ لِلقَاعِدَةِ البَيَانِيَّةِ مِنْ أَنَّ الِاسْتِعَارَةَ فِي المُشْتَقَاتِ تَبَعِيَّةٌ ، وَأَمَّا مَا يُتَبَادَرُ مِنْ كَلَامِ الشَّيْخِ المَلوِيِّ مِنْ أَنَّهَا أَصْلِيَّةٌ فَغَيْرُ ظَاهِرٍ؛ إِلَّا أَنْ يُقَالَ: إِنَّ مُخَدَّرَاتٍ مِمَّا غُلِبَتْ عَلَيْهِ الاِسْمِيَّةُ، وَالْتَحَقَ بِالجَوَامِدِ، فَلْيُفهم . قَوْلُهُ : (مُنْكَشِفَهُ) حَالٌ مِنَ المُخَدَّرَاتِ»؛ أَيْ حَالَ كَوْنِهَا مُتَّضِحَةٌ، وَلَيْسَ مَفْعُولاً ثَانِياً
Until the suns of knowledge appeared to them, they saw their hidden ones (mukhadarat) unveiled.
Then indeed 'mukhadarat' is the plural of 'mukhadara', which is a woman concealed under a veil, but the intended meaning of 'mukhadarat' here is 'hidden issues' by way of a declarative derivative metaphor. That is by likening hiddenness with the meaning of concealment, with the commonality of non-appearance in each, and the word of the likened-to is borrowed for the likened, then from it is derived 'mukhadarat' meaning 'hidden ones'. The contextual indication is the addition to the pronoun referring to knowledge or the suns as you learned. And 'sight' (ru'ya) is a reinforcement, and likewise 'unveiling' if it is literally for physical objects only. What is established that the metaphor is derivative is in accordance with the rhetorical principle that metaphor in derived terms is derivative. As for what is understood from the words of al-Mallawi that it is original, it is not apparent, unless it is said that 'mukhadarat' is among what is predominantly nominal and has become like concrete nouns, so understand. His statement: 'unveiled' is a circumstantial accusative from 'mukhadarat', meaning in the state of being clear, and it is not a second object.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is an expansion by al-Bajuri explaining the metaphor in the matn line. He begins by defining 'mukhadarat' literally as women who are veiled, then clarifies the intended meaning: here it refers to hidden issues (al-masa'il al-khafiyya) via a derivative metaphor (isti'ara taba'iyya). He details the process of metaphor: hiddenness (khafa') is likened to concealment (takhdir), both share the idea of non-appearance; the word for the vehicle (mukhadarat) is borrowed for the tenor (hidden issues), then a derived form is used. The contextual indicator (qarina) is the idafa (construct) to the pronoun referring to knowledge or the suns. Then al-Bajuri states that 'ru'ya' (seeing) is a reinforcement (tarshih) of the metaphor, and so is 'inkishaf' (unveiling) if taken literally. He affirms the principle that metaphors in derived terms are derivative, contradicting al-Mallawi who considered it original (asliyya), except if the word has become predominantly nominal like a concrete noun. Finally, he explains that 'mun-kashifah' (unveiled) is a circumstantial accusative (hal), not a second object of 'ra'a', because 'ra'a' here is visual (basarriyya) taking only one object.

Key Terms
استعارة تبعية
ترشيح
قرينة

B) The idafa (construct) to the pronoun of knowledge or suns

D) The verb 'ra'aw'

Key Takeaway
Al-Bajuri affirms that metaphors in derived terms are derivative, not original, and provides a detailed analysis of the metaphor 'mukhadarat' to illustrate the roles of qarina and tarshih.

Resolving Apparent Contradictions in Balagha: Predominant Usage and Contextual Indication
Objection and answer on sentence-type meaning association, with Taftazani's reconciliation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the principle of predominant usage (ghalabat al-isti'mal) and the distinction between original linguistic convention and contextual indication reconcile apparent contradictions in balagha texts.

Core Idea
Apparent contradictions dissolve when we distinguish original convention from contextual usage.

In this passage, an objector challenges the claim that nominal sentences indicate permanence and verbal sentences indicate renewal, arguing that both can express either meaning with contextual clues. The answer invokes predominant usage. Then a contradiction with Shaykh Abd al-Qahir arises, and al-Sa'd al-Taftazani resolves it by separating two levels of analysis. This lesson trains you to recognize and resolve such dialectical tensions, a skill essential for advanced Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial objection
The objector questions why nominal sentences are tied to permanence and verbal to renewal, since both can convey either meaning with contextual indicators (qara'in). Pinpoint the logical structure of the objection: it challenges the uniqueness of the association.
2
Extract the answer based on predominant usage
The answer appeals to 'ghalabat al-isti'mal'—predominant usage among Arabs. This is not a logical necessity but a statistical frequency. Understand that this moves the discussion from absolute semantics to customary practice.
3
Recognize the secondary contradiction
The commentator's claim about nominal sentences contradicting Shaykh Abd al-Qahir's view that they only indicate mere affirmation. Notice that this is a conflict between two authoritative statements.
4
Analyze Taftazani's resolution
Taftazani reconciles by saying the Shaykh focused on the original linguistic convention (asl al-wad'), while the other perspective considers meaning derived from contextual clues (dalala bi al-qara'in). This is a classic harmonization technique.
This distinction is widely used in usul al-fiqh and balagha to resolve conflicting statements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قِيلَ: لِمَ خُصَّتِ الاسْمِيَّةُ بِالدَّوَامِ وَالِاسْتِمْرَارِ، وَالفِعْلِيَّةُ بِالتَّجَدُّدِ، مَعَ صَلَاحِيَّةِ كُلِّ لِكُلِّ بِالقَرَائِنِ؟ أَجِيْبَ : بِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ لِغَلَبَةِ الاِسْتِعْمَالِ . وَمَا ذُكِرَ مِنْ أَنَّ الجُمْلَةَ الاِسْمِيَّةَ تَدُلُّ عَلَى الدَّوَامِ وَالِاسْتِمْرَارٍ مُخَالِفٌ لِقَوْلِ الشَّيْخِ عَبْدِ القَاهِرِ : «إِنَّهَا لَا تَدُلُّ إِلَّا عَلَى مُجَرَّدِ النُّبُوتِ»، وَدَفَعَ السَّعْدُ التَّفْتَازَانِيُّ المُخَالَفَةَ : بِأَنَّ الشَّيْخَ نَظَرَ لِأَصْلِ الوَضْعِ ، وَغَيْرَهُ نَظَرَ لِلدَّلَالَةِ بِالقَرَائِنِ.
If it is said: Why was the nominal sentence specified for permanence and continuity, and the verbal sentence for renewal, when both can be used for each with contextual indicators? The answer: Because that is due to the predominance of usage. And what was mentioned that the nominal sentence indicates permanence and continuity contradicts the saying of Shaykh Abd al-Qahir: 'It indicates nothing but mere affirmation [of the predicate].' Al-Sa'd al-Taftazani resolved the contradiction by saying: The Shaykh looked at the original linguistic convention, while others looked at indication by contextual indicators.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical exchange: an objection and its answer. The objector questions the commentator's earlier claim that the nominal sentence inherently indicates permanence and the verbal sentence inherently indicates renewal. The objector argues that both sentence types can, with the help of contextual clues, express either meaning. The answer invokes the principle of predominant usage ('ghalabat al-isti'mal') among the Arabs: although each sentence type can theoretically express either meaning, the Arabs predominantly used the nominal for stability and the verbal for change. This resolves the issue by appeal to linguistic custom. Then a secondary objection arises: the claim about the nominal sentence contradicts Shaykh Abd al-Qahir al-Jurjani's view that the nominal sentence merely affirms the predicate without implying permanence. Al-Sa'd al-Taftazani harmonizes the views by noting that al-Jurjani was considering the original linguistic convention (al-wad'), whereas the earlier statement referred to indication with the aid of contextual clues (al-qara'in). Thus, there is no real contradiction—they are discussing different levels of meaning. This illustrates how classical scholars reconciled apparent disagreements by distinguishing different analytical perspectives.

Key Terms
غلبة الاستعمال
أصل الوضع
قرينة

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradictions in classical texts can often be resolved by distinguishing between the original linguistic convention and meaning derived from contextual indicators.

The Predominant Rule of Ta'liq al-Hukm and the Role of Dhawq
Author addresses an objection about the rule of attaching ruling to derived term and clarifies the basis of praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze an objection-response sequence in a hashiya and identify how the concept of dhawq resolves ambiguity in the attachment of rulings.

Core Idea
Dhawq, not explicit wording, determines whether praise attaches to the essence or the favor.

In this passage, al-Anbabi addresses an objection against the claim that the first praise is for the essence despite the lack of explicit causation. The discussion reveals that the rule of ta'liq al-hukm is predominant, not absolute, and that intuitive linguistic sense (dhawq) plays a decisive role. Understanding this refinement is crucial for correctly interpreting praise formulas in Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What is the claim being challenged? The objection states that the first praise is not explicitly for the essence, just as it is not explicitly for the extraction, because the lam in 'Allah' is not causal.
2
Extract the grounds of the objection
On what basis is the original claim questioned? The objection uses the principle that without explicit wording, the praise cannot be considered for the essence, and points to another example (the pronoun in 'nahmaduhu') to argue inconsistency.
3
Analyze the response
How does al-Anbabi defend the original claim? He invokes dhawq: when praise is applied to the essence, it inherently pertains to the essence unless a specific cause is mentioned. Thus, the first praise is for the essence, the second for favors.
4
Evaluate the refinement
What does this add to the rule of ta'liq al-hukm? The rule is not absolute but predominant; dhawq provides a contextual understanding that overrides strict explicit wording in determining the object of praise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأنبابي في قوله : (لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ : ذَلِكَ لَيْسَ بِصَرِيحِ العِبَارَةِ، بَلْ بِاقْتِضَائِهَا) قد يقال : كما أنَّ الحمد الأوّل ليس مقابلة الإخراج بصريح العبارة، كذلك ليس هو في مقابلة الذات بصريح العبارة؛ لأنَّ اللَّام في «الله» ليست للتعليل، بل للملك أو الاستحقاق أو الاختصاص كما تقدَّم، وإنما جاء ذلك مِنَ الذوق، فلا يعتبر أيضاً كونه في مقابلة الذات، كما لم يعتبر كونه في مقابلة النعمة. ويدلُّ أيضاً لعدم اعتبار كونه في مقابلة الذات؛ لعدم التصريح بذلك عدم اعتبار كون الحمد في مقابلة في قوله : «نَحْمَدُهُ جَلَّ عَلَى الإِنْعَامِ» ؛ إذِ الضَّميرُ في نَحْمَدُهُ» عائدٌ على «الله»، فهو في مقابلة الذات؛ إلَّا أنَّه لم يصرِّح بذلك، فلذلك لم يعتبر ما ذكر . ويُجابُ : بأنه متى أوقع الحمد على الذات، كان الحمد في مقابلتها بمقتضى الذَّوق ما لم يصرِّح بأنَّه لأجل الإنعام، وإلا كان في مقابلة الإنعام، ولذلك كان الحمد في الأوّل في مقابلة الذات، وفي الثَّاني في مقابلة الإنعام فقط
Al-Anbabi said regarding his statement: 'Because we say: That is not by explicit wording, but only by its implication; and the aforementioned rule is predominant.' It may be said: Just as the first praise is not in exchange for the extraction by explicit wording, similarly it is not in exchange for the essence by explicit wording; because the lam in 'Allah' is not for causation, but for ownership, entitlement, or specificity as previously mentioned, and that came only from taste (dhawq), so it is not considered that it is in exchange for the essence, just as it is not considered that it is in exchange for the favor. And it also indicates the non-consideration of it being in exchange for the essence due to the lack of explicit mention of that, being the non-consideration of the praise being in exchange in his statement: 'We praise Him, Magnified, for the favors'; since the pronoun in 'nahmaduhu' refers to 'Allah', so it is in exchange for the essence; except that he did not explicitly state that, therefore what was mentioned was not considered. And it is answered: That whenever praise is applied to the essence, the praise is in exchange for it by virtue of taste (dhawq) unless he specifies that it is for the favor; otherwise it would be in exchange for the favor. Therefore, the first praise is in exchange for the essence, and the second is in exchange for the favor only.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) addressing an objection raised against the commentator's analysis of the opening praise. The objection argues that the first praise (al-hamd) is not explicitly stated to be in exchange for the act of bringing forth (al-ikhraj) nor for the essence (al-dhat); rather, it is only by implication (iqtida'). Similarly, the lam in 'Allah' is not for causation but for ownership, so the praise is not for the essence. The respondent counters by applying the rule of dhawq (taste): when praise is directed at the essence, it inherently pertains to the essence unless a specific cause is mentioned. Thus, the first praise (to Allah) is for the essence, and the second (for the favors) is for the favors. The rule about attaching a ruling to a derived term indicating causality is predominant (aghlabiyya), not absolute, as noted earlier. The discussion exemplifies how logical-linguistic analysis reconciles apparent ambiguities in matn wording.

Key Terms
صريح العبارة
اقتضاء
ذوق
تعليق الحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the first praise (al-hamd) considered to be in exchange for the essence rather than the favor?
A) Because it is explicitly stated with the word 'Allah'.
B) Because the lam in 'Allah' indicates causation.
C) Because when praise is applied to the essence, it is by dhawq in exchange for the essence unless a specific cause is mentioned.
D) Because the rule of ta'liq al-hukm is absolute.

Key Takeaway
Dhawq provides a contextual principle that determines the attachment of praise to essence or favor, refining the predominant rule of ta'liq al-hukm.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Analyze the following statement from a fatwa: 'We thank Allah for His guidance.' Using the concept of dhawq, explain whether the thanks is for the essence or for the specific favor of guidance, and justify your answer based on the passage.
?

Justifying Word Choice in a Matn: Nahmaduhu and Jalla
Author discusses the appropriateness of using 'nahmaduhu' instead of 'ahmaduhu' and explains the function of 'jalla'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the logical justifications for a specific philological choice in a matn, identifying the two distinct interpretations and assessing their theological coherence.

Core Idea
Every word in a matn is chosen with purpose; understanding its justification reveals the author's intent.

This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary defends the author's use of 'nahmaduhu' (we praise) instead of the expected 'ahmaduhu' (I praise). An objector claims the plural suggests self-glorification, incompatible with humility. The commentator offers two interpretations, both consistent with humility and gratitude. This lesson will walk you through the logical structure of that justification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What is the specific criticism against using 'nahmaduhu'? Locate the objector's claim: the plural 'we' either implies association with others or self-glorification, both inappropriate for a humble author.
2
Extract the first response
How does the commentator justify the plural as an expression of humility? The author says he cannot praise Allah alone, so he uses 'we' to include others, indicating his own insufficiency.
3
Extract the second response
How does the commentator justify the plural as an expression of gratitude? The author uses 'we' to magnify himself as a recipient of Allah's favor, citing the verse 'proclaim the favor of your Lord' (Ad-Duha 11).
4
Analyze theological consistency
Does each response align with the author's humility and Islamic principles? The first emphasizes humility; the second emphasizes gratitude without arrogance. Both are coherent.
5
Apply to 'jalla'
What are the two grammatical interpretations of 'jalla'? It is either an interjectory sentence (jumla i'tiradiyya) for emphasis, or a circumstantial clause (jumla haliyya) with implied 'qad' describing God's majesty.

بَقِيَ أَنَّ المُنَاسِبَ أَنْ يَقُولَ المُصَنِّفُ: «أَحْمَدُهُ بِالهَمْزَةِ، لَا بِالنُّونِ؛ لِأَنَّهَا: إِمَّا لِلمُتَكَلِّمِ مَعَ غَيْرِهِ، أَوْ لِلمُتَكَلِّمِ المُعَظْمِ نَفْسَهُ؛ وَكُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا غَيْرُ مُنَاسِبٍ هُنَا ، أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ فَظَاهِرٌ، وَأَمَّا الثَّانِي ؛ فَلِأَنَّ المُصَنِّفُ كَانَ مِنْ أَكَابِرِ المُتَوَاضِعِينَ. وَيُجَابُ : بِأَنَّهُ يَصِحُ أَنْ يَخْتَارَ الأَوَّلَ ، وَيَكُونُ المُصَنِّفُ قَدْ قَالَ ذَلِكَ احْتِفَارًا لِنَفْسِهِ عَنْ أَنْ يَسْتَقِلَّ بِحَمْدِ اللهِ تَعَالَى، فَكَأَنَّهُ يَقُولُ: الثَّنَاءُ عَلَى اللهِ تَعَالَى مَقَامٌ عَظِيمٌ لا طَاقَةَ لِي عَلَيْهِ وَحْدِي، بَلْ مَعَ غَيْرِي ، كَمَا أَشَارَ لِذَلِكَ بِتَعْبِيرِهِ بِـ «النُّونِ» التي لِلمُتَكَلّم مَعَ غَيْرِهِ. وَيَصِحُ أَنْ يَخْتَارَ الثَّانِي، وَيَكُونُ المُصَنِّفُ قَدْ قَالَ ذَلِكَ إِظْهَاراً لِتَعْظِيمِ اللهِ تَعَالَى (١) لَهُ بِتَأْهِيلِهِ (۲) لِلعِلْمِ؛ تَحَدُّنَا (۳) بِنِعْمَةِ اللهِ تَعَالَى ؛ عَمَلاً بِقَوْلِهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: ﴿وَأَمَّا بِنِعْمَةِ رَبِّكَ فَحَدِتْ ﴾ [الضحى : ١١]، كَمَا أَشَارَ لِذَلِكَ بِتَعْبِيرِهِ بِـ النُّونِ الَّتِي لِلمُتَكَلِّمِ المُعَظْمِ نَفْسَهُ، وَهَذَا لَا يُنَافِي خُضُوعَهُ وَتَوَاضُعَهُ لِمَوْلَاهُ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى . قَوْلُهُ : (جَلَّ) جُمْلَةٌ : - اعْتِرَاضِيَّةٌ فَصَدَ المُصَنِّفُ بِهَا إِنْشَاءَ التَّعْظِيم - أَوْ حَالِيَّةٌ بِتَقْدِيرِ قَدْ ، عَلَى مَا هُوَ الأَشْهَرُ مِنْ وُجُوبِ اقْتِرَانِ جُمْلَةِ الحَالِ المَاضَوِيَّةِ بِهَا لَفْظاً أَوْ تَقْدِيراً .
It remains that it would be appropriate for the author to say: 'I praise Him (ahmaduhu) with the hamza, not with the noon; because the noon is either for the speaker with others, or for the speaker glorifying himself; and both are inappropriate here. As for the first, it is obvious; as for the second, because the author was among the great humble ones.' And it is answered: That it is valid to choose the first, and the author said that out of self-abasement, not deeming himself capable of praising Allah alone, as if he says: 'Praise of Allah is a great station that I cannot accomplish alone, but with others,' as he indicated by his expression with the noon that is for the speaker with others. And it is valid to choose the second, and the author said that as a manifestation of Allah's magnifying him by qualifying him for knowledge, boasting of Allah's favor, acting upon His statement: 'And as for the favor of your Lord, proclaim [it].' (Ad-Duha 11), as he indicated by his expression with the noon that is for the speaker glorifying himself, and this does not contradict his humility and submission to his Lord, Blessed and Exalted. His statement: 'Jalla' is a sentence: — an interjectory sentence with which the author intended to initiate magnification, — or a circumstantial sentence with the implied 'qad', according to the more well-known view of the necessity of associating the past-tense circumstantial sentence with it (qad) explicitly or implicitly.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) that justifies the author's use of 'nahmaduhu' (we praise) instead of 'ahmaduhu' (I praise) and explains the word 'jalla'. The objection was that the author, being humble, should have used the singular 'I' rather than the plural 'we', which could imply self-glorification. The response provides two valid interpretations: first, the plural 'we' indicates humility, as if the author says he cannot praise Allah alone; second, it indicates gratitude for Allah's favor in granting knowledge, as per the verse 'proclaim the favor of your Lord', and this does not contradict humility. Then the text analyzes 'jalla' as either an interjectory sentence (for initiating magnification) or a circumstantial clause (with implied 'qad') describing the state of the praised. This detailed grammatical and rhetorical analysis shows how every word in the matn is carefully chosen and justified according to linguistic and theological principles.

جَلَّ
جملة اعتراضية
جملة حالية

Critically Evaluating Grammatical Interpretations of 'جلَّ' in al-Sullam's Opening
Commentator examines and refutes claims that 'جلَّ' is a ḥāl or ṣifa, and argues for iʿtirāḍiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate competing grammatical analyses (ḥāl, ṣifa, iʿtirāḍiyya, badal) for a word in a classical logic text and argue why one is preferred.

Core Idea
Grammar shapes meaning in logic; a mistaken parsing undermines the logical argument.

In al-Sullam's opening line, the word 'جلَّ' (Exalted) can be interpreted in several grammatical ways. The commentator systematically examines each possibility, showing how grammatical choices affect the logical force of the praise. This lesson guides you through his method of critical refinement, equipping you to handle similar ambiguous terms in Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the candidate analyses
List all possible grammatical roles for 'جلَّ' that the commentator considers: it could be a ḥāl (circumstantial accusative), a ṣifa (adjective describing the pronoun), an iʿtirāḍiyya (parenthetical), or even a badal (substitution).
These are the standard categories for a non-integrated clause.
2
Assess the ḥāl analysis
Understand the objection: a ḥāl restricts the verb (operator). Making praise conditioned by a specific state lowers its virtue compared to absolute praise. Even if the ḥāl is 'lāzima' (inseparable), the restriction remains.
The commentator dismisses this because unrestricted praise is more complete.
3
Assess the ṣifa analysis
Check the linguistic evidence: does any grammarian permit describing a third-person pronoun with a full sentence? The commentator says no. The examples from al-Kisā'ī involve single definite words, not sentences, and those are usually explained as badal by the majority.
This refutation relies on consensus of grammarians.
4
Evaluate the iʿtirāḍiyya analysis
Consider al-Malawi's objection: a parenthetical cannot be replaced by a single word. The reply is that the replacement only works if the sentence is a ḥāl, not if it is parenthetical. Many sentences can serve both roles; the possibility of being a ḥāl does not exclude it from being parenthetical.
The commentator notes that al-Malawi himself retracted this objection.
5
Decide the preferred analysis
Based on the refutations and the reply, the commentator concludes that making 'جلَّ' iʿtirāḍiyya is 'awlā' (more appropriate). This aligns with the preference for unrestricted praise and avoids grammatical difficulties.
This is the lesson's main takeaway: grammatical reasoning supports the parenthetical reading.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَوْ صِفَةٌ لِلضَّمِيرِ عَلَى مَذْهَبِ مَنْ يُجِيزُ وَصْفَ الضَّمِيرِ. عَلَى جَعْلِهَا حَالِيَّةٌ : أَنَّ الحَالَ قَيْدٌ فِي عَامِلِهَا ، فَيَقْتَضِي ذَلِكَ تَقْبِيدُ الحَمْدِ بِتِلْكَ الحَالِ، وَلَا نَظَرَ لِكَوْنِ الحَالِ هُنَا لَازِمَةٌ لِأَنَّ الحَمْدَ المُطْلَقَ أَفْضَلُ مِنَ الحَمْدِ المُقَيَّدِ بِوَصْفٍ ، كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ . وَيُرَدُّ عَلَى جَعْلِهَا صِفَةٌ : أَنَّا لَمْ نَطَلِعْ فِي كُتُبِ النَّحْوِ عَلَى أَنَّ أَحَداً يُجِيزُ وَصْفَ ضَمِيرِ الغَيْبَةِ الرَّاجِع إِلَى مُعَيَّنٍ بِجُمْلَةٍ ، وَالأَمْيْلَةُ الَّتِي نَقَلَتْ عَنِ الكِسَائِيِّ إِجَازَةَ وَصْفِ الضَّمِيرِ فِيهَا، لَيْسَ فِيهَا إِلَّا وَصْفُهُ بِمُفْرَدٍ مَعْرِفَةٍ ; نَحْوُ : «اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَيْهِ الرَّؤوفِ الرَّحِيمِ» وَنَحْوُ : «لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ العَزِيزُ الرَّحِيمُ» ، وَالجُمْهُورُ عَلَى أَنَّ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ عَلَى البَدَلِ. وَمِنْ هَذَا تَعْلَمُ وَجْهَ قَوْلِ بَعْضِهِمْ : بِأَنَّ جَعْلَهَا اعْتِرَاضِيَّةً أَوْلَى . وَمَا فِي بَعْضِ نُسَخِ الشَّرْحِ الصَّغِيرِ لِلشَّيْخ المَلَّوِيِّ مِنْ أَنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُ أَنْ تَكُونَ اعْتِرَاضِيَّةٌ ; لأَنَّ المُفْرَدَ يَحِلُّ مَحَلَّهَا ، وَلَا كَذَلِكَ الاِعْتِرَاضِيَّةُ» ; بُحِثَ فِيهِ : بِأَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا يَحِلُّ الْمُفْرَدُ مَحَلَّهَا عَلَى تَقْدِيرِ يَمْنَعُ مِنْ أَنَّهَا حَالٌ، لَا عَلَى تَقْدِيرِ أَنَّهَا اعْتِرَاضِيَّةٌ، وَحُلُولُ المُفْرَدِ مَحَلَّهَا عَلَى تَقْدِيرِ أَنَّهَا حَالٌ لَا صِحَّةِ كَوْنِهَا اعْتِرَاضِيَّةٌ كَمَا فِي سَائِرِ الجُمَلِ المُحْتَمِلَةِ لِلاعْتِرَاضِ وَالحَالِ، وَلِهَذَا نُقِلَ عَنِ الشَّيْخِ أَنَّهُ رَجَعَ عَنْ هَذِهِ العِبَارَةِ، وَضَرَبَ عَلَيْهَا بِخَطَّهِ.
Or a description of the pronoun according to the school of those who permit describing the pronoun. Regarding making it a hāl: that the hāl is a restriction in its operator, so that necessitates restricting the praise with that state, and no consideration is given to the state here being necessary because the absolute praise is more virtuous than the praise restricted by a description, as some mentioned. And it is refuted regarding making it a description: that we have not come across in the books of grammar that anyone permits describing a third-person pronoun referring to a specific entity with a sentence, and the examples that were transmitted from al-Kisa'i permitting describing the pronoun in them only include describing it with a definite single word, like 'O Allah, bless him, the Merciful, the Compassionate,' and like 'There is no god but He, the Mighty, the Merciful,' and the majority consider such to be substitution (badal). From this you know the aspect of the saying of some that making it parenthetical (i'tiradi) is more appropriate. And what is in some copies of the Small Commentary by al-Malawi that it is not valid to be parenthetical because a single word can replace it, but not so the parenthetical, it was examined: that the single word replaces it only on the assumption that it prevents it from being a hāl, not on the assumption that it is parenthetical, and the replacement of the single word for it on the assumption that it is a hāl does not prove its being parenthetical, as in all sentences that admit of being parenthetical or a hāl, and for this it was transmitted from the Shaykh that he retracted this expression and struck it out with his own hand.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the grammatical status of the word 'جلَّ' (meaning 'Great' or 'Exalted') in the opening line of al-Sullam's poem. The commentator first notes the possibility that it is a صفة (adjective) describing the pronoun in 'نَحْمَدُهُ', according to those who permit describing a pronoun. Then he examines the claim that it is a حال (hāl, circumstantial accusative). The objection to that is that a hāl restricts its operator, which here would restrict the praise to that specific state, but absolute praise is better than restricted praise. He dismisses the idea that the hāl is necessary (لازمة) because it would still restrict. Then he refutes the claim that it is a صفة by arguing that no grammarian permits describing a third-person pronoun with a sentence; the examples attributed to al-Kisa'i only allow description with a single definite word, and even those are considered by the majority to be بدَل (substitution), not صفة. From this, the commentator concludes that making it اعتراضية (parenthetical) is more appropriate. He then examines an objection from al-Malawi's commentary that it cannot be parenthetical because a single word (like 'جلَّ' itself) can replace the sentence, which would not hold for a parenthetical. The reply is that the single word replaces it only if the sentence is assumed to be a hāl, not if it is parenthetical, and this does not prove it cannot be parenthetical, as many sentences can be either. The commentator then notes that the Shaykh himself retracted this statement. This passage shows the meticulous grammatical reasoning typical of Arabic rhetoric and grammar, applied to the logical text of al-Sullam.

صِفَة
اعْتِرَاضِيَّة
ضَمِير
بَدَل

Key Takeaway
In analyzing a word's grammatical role in a classical text, systematically eliminate impossible or inferior interpretations using linguistic evidence and logical consequences, then adopt the one that best fits the author's intent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
In a juristic text (e.g., al-Mukhtaṣar of Khalīl), a phrase like 'وَلا تَجُوزُ الصَّلاَةُ إِلاَّ بِطَهَارَةٍ' contains 'إِلاَّ' which can be interpreted as istithnā' mufarragħ or istithnā' muttaṣil. Use the critical refinement approach to decide which analysis yields the correct legal scope.

Understanding 'عَلَى' and the Singular 'نِعْمَة'
Grammatical analysis of 'عَلَى' and singular 'نِعْمَة'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the meaning of 'عَلَى' as 'lam al-ta'lil' and explain why the author used the singular 'نِعْمَة' instead of the dual in the opening line of al-Sullam.

Core Idea
Prepositions carry logical weight; word choice reveals deeper meaning.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks the grammar of the opening words of al-Sullam. He shows that the preposition 'عَلَى' here does not mean 'upon' but indicates causation, similar to its use in the Quran. He also addresses the puzzle of why the author wrote 'بِنِعْمَةِ الإِيمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ' (with the blessing of faith and Islam) using the singular 'blessing' rather than the dual 'two blessings'. Understanding these choices sharpens your ability to read classical texts with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preposition 'عَلَى' and its context
Locate the word 'عَلَى' in the source text. The commentator explains that here it means 'for the sake of' (لِأَجْلِ), i.e., lam al-ta'lil (the lam of causation). This is not the primary meaning of 'عَلَى', so recognize that context determines meaning.
The Quranic example {وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا اللهَ عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ} supports this interpretation.
2
Examine the idafa construction of 'نِعْمَة'
The phrase 'بِنِعْمَةِ الإِيمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ' has a singular possessed noun 'نِعْمَة' governing two possessed items ('الإِيمَانِ' and 'الإِسْلَامِ'). Note that the expected form would be dual: 'بِنِعْمَتَيْ الإِيمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ'. The commentator offers two justifications.
The singular noun in idafa can be general (يَعُمُّ) or the second possessed noun is deleted (حَذَفَ المُضَافَ).
3
Apply the justification to similar Arabic expressions
Think of other examples where a singular noun before multiple items is used for brevity or generality, e.g., 'صِيَامِ رَمَضَانَ وَشَوَّالَ' (the fasting of Ramadan and Shawwal). This step reinforces the grammatical principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَ : قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى الإِنْعَامِ أَيْ: لِأَجْلِ الإِنْعَامِ ، فَ عَلَى بِمَعْنَى : لَامِ التَّعْلِيلِ، كَمَا فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: {وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا اللهَ عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ} [البقرة : ١٨٥] . قَوْلُهُ : (بِنِعْمَةِ الإِيمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ) الجَارُّ وَالمَجْرُورُ فِيهِ مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِـ «الإِنْعَامِ، وَإِضَافَةُ «نِعْمَة» لِمَا بَعْدَهَا لِلبَيَانِ . وَكَانَ مُقْتَضَى الظَّاهِرِ أَنْ يَقُولَ: بِنِعْمَتَ الإِيْمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ ; إِلَّا أَنْ يُقَالَ : المُفْرَدُ المُضَافُ يَعُمُّ ، أَوْ يُقَالُ : حَذَفَ المُضَافَ مِنَ الثَّانِي لِدَلَالَتِهِ فِي الأَوَّلِ عَلَيْهِ، وَالأَصْلُ : بِنِعْمَةِ الإِيْمَانِ وَنِعْمَةِ الإِسْلَامِ. وَإِنَّمَا جَمَعَ المُصَنِّفُ بَيْنَ الإِيْمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ مَعَ تَلَازُمِهِمَا وُجُوداً - بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُ مِنْ وُجُودِ الإِيمَانِ فِي شَخْصٍ وُجُودُ الإِسْلَامِ فِيهِ، وَبِالعَكْسِ ; لِتَغَابِرِهِمَا مَنْهُوماً وَمَا صَدَقاً : أَمَّا الأَوَّلُ، فَلِأَنَّ : - مَنْهُومَ الإِيمَانِ لُغَةٌ : مُطْلَقُ التَصْدِيقِ، وَمِنْهُ : {وَمَا أَنتَ بِمُؤْمِنٍ لَّنَا} [يوسف: ١٧] .
Then: His statement: 'upon the bestowing' i.e., for the sake of the bestowing, so 'upon' means the lam of causation, as in His statement: 'and that you magnify Allah for what He has guided you.' His statement: 'with the blessing of faith and Islam': the preposition and its object are attached to 'the bestowing', and the addition of 'blessing' to what follows is for clarification. And the apparent requirement would be to say: 'with the two blessings of faith and Islam'; except that it is said: the singular possessed noun is general, or it is said: the possessed noun was deleted from the second due to the indication of the first upon it, and the original is: 'with the blessing of faith and the blessing of Islam'. And the author only combined faith and Islam despite their coexisting in existence—meaning that the existence of faith in a person necessitates the existence of Islam in him, and vice versa—due to their difference in concept and extension: as for the first (concept), because the linguistic concept of faith is absolute assent, and from this is His statement: 'And you are not a believer (mu'min) for us.'
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the author's commentary on the opening line of al-Sullam, specifically analyzing the phrase 'عَلَى الإِنْعَامِ بِنِعْمَةِ الإِيمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ'. The commentator first explains that 'عَلَى' here means 'for the sake of' (لام التعليل), citing the Quranic verse {وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا اللهَ عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ} as evidence. Then he discusses 'بِنِعْمَةِ الإِيمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ': the prepositional phrase is attached to 'الإنعام', and the idafa (possessive construction) of 'نِعْمَة' is for clarification (بيان). He notes that the expected form would be the dual 'بِنِعْمَتَيْ' (with two blessings), but the singular 'نِعْمَة' is used either because the singular in idafa is general or because the possessed noun is deleted from the second phrase, with the original being 'بِنِعْمَةِ الإِيمَانِ وَنِعْمَةِ الإِسْلَامِ'. The commentator then addresses why the author mentions both faith (ٍإيمان) and Islam (إسلام) even though they coexist (تلازم وجوداً): one implies the other. The reason is that they differ in concept (مفهوم) and extension (ماصدق). He gives the example: the linguistic concept of faith is 'absolute assent' (مطلق التصديق), citing the verse {وَمَا أَنتَ بِمُؤْمِنٍ لَّنَا} where 'mu'min' means 'assenting'. Thus, mentioning both highlights the distinct meanings despite their inseparability in reality.

Key Terms
إِنْعَام
نِعْمَة
عَلَى
لَامُ التَّعْلِيلِ
إِضَافَة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the author made a grammatical mistake.
B) Because the singular possessed noun is general or the second possessed noun is deleted.
C) Because 'نِعْمَة' refers only to faith, not Islam.
D) Because Islam is not a blessing.

Key Takeaway
The use of singular 'نِعْمَة' is either due to generality or ellipsis, and 'عَلَى' indicates causation.

Why Mention Both Faith and Islam Despite Their Coexistence
Explanation of why coexistent terms are both mentioned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conceptual difference (taghabur fi al-mafhum) and existential coexistence (talazum wujudi) and explain why two coexistent terms like iman and islam are both mentioned.

Core Idea
Concepts are distinct even when their referents are inseparable.

The author of al-Sullam mentions both 'الإيمان' (faith) and 'الإسلام' (submission) in the same phrase, even though they are necessarily coexistent: one cannot exist without the other. The commentator clarifies that this is not redundant because the two terms differ in concept (مفهوم) and extension (ماصدق). This logical insight is crucial for understanding how scholars use precise terminology in theology and law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms 'الإيمان' and 'الإسلام' and their relationship
Read the passage and note that the commentator says they 'تلازماً وجوداً' (coexist in existence). That means if one is present, the other is necessarily present. This is a logical relationship of mutual entailment.
Talazum does not imply sameness; it implies necessary coexistence.
2
Distinguish between concept (mafhum) and extension (masdaq)
The commentator says they differ 'منهوماً و ما صدقاً'. Concept is the mental definition or meaning; extension is the set of individuals to which the term applies. Here, the concepts of iman and islam are different, but their extensions are identical in reality (every believer is a submitter and vice versa).
Example: 'water' and 'H2O' have the same extension but different concepts.
3
Examine the given concept of iman
The commentator defines the linguistic concept of iman as 'absolute assent' (مطلق التصديق), citing the Quranic verse {وَمَا أَنتَ بِمُؤْمِنٍ لَّنَا}. This is a minimal definition. Islam is not explicitly defined here, but by contrast, it implies outward submission.
In kalam, iman often includes inner conviction plus works, but here it is purely linguistic.
4
Apply the distinction to other theological pairs
Think of terms like 'khashyah' (fear) and 'taqwa' (piety) or 'fard' and 'wajib'. They often coexist but have distinct concepts. This skill helps avoid confusion in debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَ : قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى الإِنْعَامِ أَيْ: لِأَجْلِ الإِنْعَامِ ، فَ عَلَى بِمَعْنَى : لَامِ التَّعْلِيلِ، كَمَا فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: {وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا اللهَ عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ} [البقرة : ١٨٥] . قَوْلُهُ : (بِنِعْمَةِ الإِيمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ) الجَارُّ وَالمَجْرُورُ فِيهِ مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِـ «الإِنْعَامِ، وَإِضَافَةُ «نِعْمَة» لِمَا بَعْدَهَا لِلبَيَانِ . وَكَانَ مُقْتَضَى الظَّاهِرِ أَنْ يَقُولَ: بِنِعْمَتَ الإِيْمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ ; إِلَّا أَنْ يُقَالَ : المُفْرَدُ المُضَافُ يَعُمُّ ، أَوْ يُقَالُ : حَذَفَ المُضَافَ مِنَ الثَّانِي لِدَلَالَتِهِ فِي الأَوَّلِ عَلَيْهِ، وَالأَصْلُ : بِنِعْمَةِ الإِيْمَانِ وَنِعْمَةِ الإِسْلَامِ. وَإِنَّمَا جَمَعَ المُصَنِّفُ بَيْنَ الإِيْمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ مَعَ تَلَازُمِهِمَا وُجُوداً - بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُ مِنْ وُجُودِ الإِيمَانِ فِي شَخْصٍ وُجُودُ الإِسْلَامِ فِيهِ، وَبِالعَكْسِ ; لِتَغَابِرِهِمَا مَنْهُوماً وَمَا صَدَقاً : أَمَّا الأَوَّلُ، فَلِأَنَّ : - مَنْهُومَ الإِيمَانِ لُغَةٌ : مُطْلَقُ التَصْدِيقِ، وَمِنْهُ : {وَمَا أَنتَ بِمُؤْمِنٍ لَّنَا} [يوسف: ١٧] .
Then: His statement: 'upon the bestowing' i.e., for the sake of the bestowing, so 'upon' means the lam of causation, as in His statement: 'and that you magnify Allah for what He has guided you.' His statement: 'with the blessing of faith and Islam': the preposition and its object are attached to 'the bestowing', and the addition of 'blessing' to what follows is for clarification. And the apparent requirement would be to say: 'with the two blessings of faith and Islam'; except that it is said: the singular possessed noun is general, or it is said: the possessed noun was deleted from the second due to the indication of the first upon it, and the original is: 'with the blessing of faith and the blessing of Islam'. Resolving Apparent Restriction: Two Interpretations of the Ba'
Author addresses the apparent restriction of the Prophet's mission and provides two interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical problem in a restrictive construction and reconstruct two interpretations that resolve the apparent contradiction between the wording and the theological doctrine.

Core Idea
The ba' of restriction can shift its grammatical object to preserve theological truth.

In this passage, al-Bajuri tackles a puzzling phrase: 'He singled us out with the best of those who were sent.' The word 'singled out' (khassa) seems to imply the Prophet was sent only to us. But we know he was sent to all nations. Al-Bajuri explains that the preposition ba' determines the direction of restriction, and provides two grammatical solutions that reconcile the wording with the universal mission of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent implication
Read the phrase 'khassana bi khayri man ursila' literally. The word 'khassa' (singled out) combined with the ba' suggests restriction. If the ba' enters upon the restricted (al-maqsour), the meaning is that the Prophet is restricted to us—he is only our prophet.
This is the dominant usage of ba' in qasr constructions.
2
Detect the contradiction
The apparent implication contradicts the known doctrine that the Prophet was sent to all nations, including previous ones. The author states that the truth is that he was sent to earlier nations, with other prophets as his deputies.
The contradiction triggers the need for reinterpretation.
3
Examine the first solution (ba' on maqsour 'alayhi)
Al-Bajuri proposes that the ba' here enters upon the one restricted to (al-maqsour 'alayhi), not the restricted. This means Allah restricted us (the Muslims) to the Prophet—we must follow him exclusively, not other messengers. This preserves his universality.
This solution requires a departure from the dominant usage.
4
Examine the second solution (ba' on maqsour with direct vs indirect)
Alternatively, the ba' enters upon the restricted as usual, but 'singled out' means Allah directly sent him to us without intermediary. He was also sent to other nations indirectly through other prophets, as the al-Burdah verse illustrates: other prophets reflect his light.
This solution keeps the dominant grammatical structure.
5
Compare the two solutions
Both solutions affirm the Prophet's universal mission. The first shifts the referent of restriction; the second distinguishes direct from indirect sending. They show how grammatical analysis can reconcile wording with doctrine.
The author considers the first solution the 'best' among several answers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِذَا عَلِمْتَ ذَلِكَ عَلِمْتَ أَنَّ المُتَبَادَرَ مِنْ كَلَام المُصَنِّفِ دُخُولُهَا عَلَى المَقْصُورِ كَمَا هُوَ الغَالِبُ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ ، فَمُقْتَضَاهُ أَنَّهُ مَقْصُورٌ عَلَيْنَا لَا يَتَعَدَّانَا إِلَى غَيْرِنَا ، وَلَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ ؛ لِأَنَّ الحَقَّ أَنَّهُ مُرْسَلٌ لِلأُمَمِ السَّابِقَةِ ؛ غَايَةُ الأَمْرِ أَنَّ الرُّسُلَ نُوَّابٌ عَنْهُ ، كَمَا يُشِيرُ لِذَلِكَ قَوْلُ صَاحِبِ البُرْدَةِ : [ من البسيط] فَإِنَّهُ شَمْسُ فَضْلِ هُمْ كَوَاكِبُهَا يُظْهِرْنَ أَنْوَارَهَا لِلنَّاسِ فِي الظُّلَمِ وَأُجِيْبَ عَنْهُ بِأَجْوِبَةٍ ؛ أَحْسَنُهَا : أَنَّ البَاءَ هُنَا دَاخِلَةٌ عَلَى المَقْصُورِ عَلَيْهِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ خِلَافَ الغَالِبِ عَلَى مَا تَقَدَّمَ، وَالمَعْنَى عَلَيْهِ : أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى قَصَرَنَا عَلَيْهِ ، لَا نَتَجَاوَزُهُ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ مِنَ الرُّسُلِ. أَوْ أَنَّهَا دَاخِلَةٌ عَلَى المَقْصُورِ كَمَا هُوَ الغَالِبُ، لَكِنَّ المُرَادَ أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى خَصَّنَا بِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مِنْ حَيْثُ إِرْسَالُهُ لَنَا بِطَرِيقِ المُبَاشَرَةِ، فَلَا يُنَافِي أَنَّهُ أُرْسِلَ أَيْضاً لِغَيْرِنَا مِنَ الْأُمَمِ لَكِنْ بِوَاسِطَةِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ.
When you know that, you know that what is apparent from the author's speech is that it (the ba') enters upon the restricted (al-maqsour), as is dominant according to what has passed, so its implication is that he (the Prophet) is restricted to us, not extending to others. But that is not so, because the truth is that he was sent to previous nations; the point is that the messengers are his deputies, as indicated by the saying of the author of al-Burdah: 'Indeed, he is a sun of virtue, they (i.e., the other prophets) are its planets, revealing its lights to people in darkness.' And it was answered with several answers; the best of them is that the ba' here enters upon the one restricted to (al-maqsour 'alayhi), even if it is contrary to the dominant according to what preceded, and the meaning accordingly is that Allah restricted us to him, we do not go beyond him to other messengers. Or that it enters upon the restricted as is dominant, but the intended meaning is that Allah singled us out with him, peace be upon him, by way of his being sent to us directly, so it does not contradict that he was also sent to other nations but through the mediation of messengers, may peace and blessings be upon him and them.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical commentary on a line of poetry (the matn) praising the Prophet. The author, al-Bajuri, first identifies a potential problem: the apparent meaning of the phrase 'خصنا بخير من أرسلا' (He singled us out with the best of those who were sent) seems to imply that the Prophet was sent only to the Muslim community ('restricted to us'), because the preposition 'ba' typically enters upon the restricted (al-maqsour) in constructions of restriction (qasr). However, this contradicts the theological truth that the Prophet was sent to all nations, including previous ones. To resolve this, al-Bajuri quotes a line from al-Burdah comparing the Prophet to the sun and other prophets to planets that reflect his light, illustrating that the Prophet's message reaches others through the intermediary prophets. Then he provides two answers. The first answer: the ba' here exceptionally enters upon the one restricted to (al-maqsour 'alayhi), meaning that Allah restricted us (the Muslims) to him, i.e., we are bound to follow him alone, not other messengers. This interpretation preserves the universal mission of the Prophet while explaining the 'restriction' as pertaining to the community's obligation. The second answer: the ba' enters upon the restricted as usual, but the intended meaning is that Allah directly sent him to us (the Muslim community) without intermediary, which does not negate that he was also sent to other nations through other prophets. Both solutions maintain the Prophet's universality while explaining the restrictive wording.

Key Terms
الباء
المقصور
المقصور عليه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first answer, what does the phrase 'خصنا بخير من أرسلا' mean?
A) Allah restricted the Prophet to us, so he is only our prophet.
B) Allah restricted us to the Prophet, meaning we must follow him and not other messengers.
C) Allah made the Prophet the best of all creation, but not sent to others.
D) The Prophet was sent directly to all nations without any intermediary.

Key Takeaway
The apparent restriction in wording can be reinterpreted without contradicting the universal message by analyzing the grammatical function of the preposition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the verse 'إِنَّمَا أَنْتَ مُنْذِرُ مَنْ يَخْشَاهَا' (You are only a warner for those who fear it). Determine whether the restriction applies to the warner or the warned. Using the logic of the two solutions from al-Bajuri, explain what the verse means and how it can be reconciled with the Prophet's universal message.
?

Condition for Omitting the Genitive Pronoun After a Preposition
Al-Anbabi refutes a potential objection about the omitted pronoun in the phrase 'على الذي قصروا'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition for omitting a genitive pronoun (العائد المجرور) after a preposition in Arabic grammar and apply it to the phrase 'على الذي قصروا'.

Core Idea
A pronoun cannot be omitted from a preposition unless both prepositions share the same governing verb.

In Arabic grammar, omitting a pronoun after a preposition is not arbitrary; strict conditions apply. Al-Anbabi refutes a potential misinterpretation of the phrase 'على الذي قصروا' by showing that the required condition—that both prepositions be governed by the same verb—is violated. This lesson will walk you through his argument and the underlying grammatical rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and the objection
Locate the phrase 'على الذي قد قصروا' in the passage. The objection is that it could mean 'on the one they have restricted [upon]', with the pronoun 'عليه' omitted after 'على'.
2
Recall the condition for dropping the genitive pronoun
The condition is that the two prepositions (the one present and the one implied) must be attached to the same governing word (متعلق الحرفين واحد). Here, the explicit 'على' is governed by 'قصروا' (they restricted), but the implied 'على' would be governed by 'دخول' (entry) from earlier context.
3
Apply the condition to the objection
Since the governing words differ ('دخول' vs 'قصروا'), the condition fails. Therefore, the pronoun cannot be omitted.
4
Determine the correct reading
Al-Anbabi concludes that the pronoun must be in the accusative (منصوب), yielding 'على الذي قصروه' (on the one they restricted), i.e., the restricted (المقصور) rather than the one restricted to.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأنبابي ولا يجاب بأنه جرى على ما نقله وأنَّ قوله : عَلَى الَّذِي قَدْ قَصَرُوا معناه : على الذي قد قصروا سم، عليه، وهو المقصور عليه؛ لأنَّه يلزم حذف العائد المجرور من غير وجود الشُّروط؛ إذ مِن جملتها أن يتحد متعلق الحرفين، وهنا لم يتحدا؛ إذ متعلَّق الأوّل: دخول والثَّاني : قصروا فيتعيَّن أنَّ العائد هنا منصوب؛ أي: على الذي قصروه، وهو المقصور.
Al-Anbabi: And it cannot be answered that it (the construction) follows what he transmitted, and that his saying: 'عَلَى الَّذِي قَدْ قَصَرُوا' means 'on the one they have restricted [upon]' (i.e., the one restricted to), because that would require dropping the prepositional object pronoun without fulfilling the conditions; among these conditions is that the two prepositions share the same governing word, but here they do not share it, since the first is governed by 'dakhala' and the second by 'qassaru'. So it is determined that the returning pronoun here is in the accusative: i.e., 'on the one they restricted', and that is the restricted (al-maqsour).
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) by al-Anbabi on a previous commentary. He discusses a potential objection to the interpretation of the phrase 'على الذي قد قصروا' (on the one they have restricted). The objection would be that the construction means 'on the one they have restricted [upon]', taking the pronoun as implied after the preposition 'على'. Al-Anbabi rejects this answer because it would require omitting the prepositional object pronoun (al-'a'id al-majrur) without satisfying the grammatical conditions. One condition is that the two prepositions (here, the implicit 'على' and the explicit 'على') must be governed by the same verb. However, the first 'على' is governed by 'دخول' (entry) and the second by 'قصروا' (they restricted). Since the governing words differ, the pronoun cannot be dropped. Therefore, the correct reading is that the pronoun is in the accusative, meaning 'on the one they restricted', referring to the restricted (al-maqsour), not the one restricted to (al-maqsour 'alayhi). This clarifies the grammatical point and supports a particular interpretation of the matn.

Key Terms
العائد المجرور
متعلق الحرفين
الشروط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The two prepositions must be identical in spelling.
B) The two prepositions must share the same governing verb.
C) The pronoun must be masculine singular.
D) The phrase must be a well-known expression.

Key Takeaway
Omitting a genitive pronoun after a preposition requires that both prepositions share the same governing verb; otherwise, the pronoun must appear explicitly.

The Elative Form and the Cause of the Prophet's Superiority
Grammatical and theological expansion on two praise phrases for the Prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the grammatical derivation of an elative form in Arabic and distinguish the two theological positions on the cause of the Prophet's superiority as presented in al-Bajuri's commentary.

Core Idea
The Prophet's excellence is by divine decree, not his own merits—an Ash'ari principle.

In this passage, al-Bajuri unpacks two lines praising the Prophet, combining grammatical analysis with a theological debate. You will learn how the elative form 'khayr' is derived and why the scope of 'man' changes between the two phrases. Then you will engage with the key Ash'ari position that the Prophet's superiority is solely by Allah's preference, not his personal merits, and see how this refutes al-Zamakhshari's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the elative form and its derivation
Find 'خَيْر' in the Arabic and note al-Bajuri's explanation that its original is 'أَخْيَرُ', with a vowel shift and hamza deletion. This is a standard process for elatives in Arabic grammar.
Elative = comparative/superlative form (أفعل تفضيل).
2
Analyze the scope of 'من' in each phrase
In the first phrase, 'من' applies to a prophet or human, not specifically a messenger, to avoid redundancy with 'أرسل'. In the second, 'من' applies to any human, making it more general. Compare the two to see how the praise broadens.
This shows the precision of Arabic in theological expression.
3
Extract the theological debate on superiority
Al-Bajuri presents two views: (1) superiority due to the Prophet's own merits (mazaya), (2) superiority by Allah's preference (tafdil Allah). He endorses the second as the position of the verifiers, citing al-Sanusi.
This is a key Ash'ari doctrine: God's acts are not caused by creaturely qualities.
4
Note the refutation of al-Zamakhshari
Al-Anbabi adds that the conjunction in the second phrase also serves to refute al-Zamakhshari's claim that Gabriel is superior to the Prophet. The broader scope of 'من' includes Gabriel, so the Prophet is best of all humans, not just prophets.
This shows how grammatical details can have theological ramifications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا) «خَيْر»: أَفْعُلُ تَفْضِيل، فَأَصْلُهُ: «أَخْيَرُ» نُقِلَتْ حَرَكَةُ اليَاءِ إِلَى السَّاكِنِ قَبْلَهَا، وَحُذِفَتْ مِنْهُ الهَمْزَةُ تَخْفِيفاً ، وَمَنْ وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى نَبِيٍّ أَوْ إِنْسَانٍ، لَا عَلَى رَسُولٍ؛ لِئَلَّا يَضِيعَ قَوْلُهُ : «قَدْ أُرْسَلَا» . وَاخْتُلِفَ هَلْ خَيرِيَّتُهُ بِسَبَبِ مَزَايَاهُ أَوْ لَا ، بَلْ بِتَفْضِيلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لَهُ؟ وَالثَّانِي هُوَ كَلَامُ أَهْلِ التَّحْقِيقِ مِنْ أَئِمَّةِ الكَلَامِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ السَّنُوسِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ صُغْرَى الصُّغُرَى. قَوْلُهُ : (وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلا) «مَنْ هُنَا وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى إِنْسَانٍ»؛ أَعَمُّ مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ رَسُولاً أَوْ لَا ، صِفَتُهُ أَنَّهُ جَمَعَ المَرَاتِبَ العَالِيَةَ، فَهَذَا أَعَمُّ مِمَّا قَبْلَهُ. والعُلَا جَمْعُ: «عُلْيَا) - بِالضَّمِّ وَالقَصْرِ ، وَهِيَ كَـ: «العَلْيَاءِ» ـ بِالفَتْحِ وَالمَدِّ - ؛ ضِدُّ : السُّفْلَى». قَوْلُهُ : (مُحَمَّدٍ) المُنَاسِبُ لِلتَّعْظِيمِ : رَفْعُهُ؛ عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَرٌ لِمُبْتَدَأَ مَحْذُوفٍ، وَالجُمْلَةُ مُسْتَانَفَةٌ كَالجُمْلَةِ السَّابِقَةِ . الأنبابي قوله : (فَهَذَا أَعَمُّ مِمَّا قَبْلَهُ) وفي العطف زيادةً على فائدة التَّعميم : الإشارة لردّ ما ذهب إليه الزمخشري من تفضيل جبريل على نبينا وعلى غيره مِنَ الأنبياء عليه وعليهم أفضل الصَّلاة وأتم التسليم.
His saying: 'بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا' (With the best of those who were sent): 'خَيْر' is an elative (af'ul tafdil); its original is 'أَخْيَرُ'; the vowel of the ya' was moved to the preceding consonant, and the hamza was dropped for ease. 'مَنْ' here applies to a prophet or a human being, not specifically a messenger, so that his saying 'قَدْ أُرْسَلَا' (has been sent) does not become meaningless. And it is debated whether his superiority (khayriyya) is due to his own merits or rather due to Allah's preference of him? The second is the view of the verifiers among the theologians, as al-Sanusi said in his commentary on al-Sughra al-Sughra. His saying: 'وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلا' (And the best of those who attained the high stations): 'مَنْ' here applies to a human being, more general than being a messenger or not; his description is that he gathered the high ranks, so this is more general than what preceded. 'العُلَا' is the plural of 'عُلْيَا' (with damm and qasr), and it is like 'العَلْيَاء' (with fatha and madd); its opposite is 'السُّفْلَى'. His saying: 'مُحَمَّدٍ' (Muhammad): what is appropriate for glorification is that it be in the nominative, as the predicate of a deleted subject, and the sentence is a resumption like the previous sentence. Al-Anbabi said: 'His saying: (فَهَذَا أَعَمُّ مِمَّا قَبْلَهُ) and the conjunction, in addition to the benefit of generalization, indicates a refutation of what al-Zamakhshari held regarding the preferability of Gabriel over our Prophet and over other prophets — may the best prayers and complete salutations be upon him and them.'
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on two lines of the matn describing the Prophet. Al-Bajuri begins with the phrase 'بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا' (with the best of those who were sent). He gives a grammatical analysis: 'خَيْر' is an elative form (af'ul tafdil), originally 'أَخْيَرُ', with a phonetic change. The relative pronoun 'مَنْ' refers to a prophet or a human being, not specifically a 'messenger' (rasul), because if it were restricted to messengers, the subsequent word 'أُرْسَلَا' (he was sent) would be redundant. Then he raises a theological question: Is the Prophet's superiority (khayriyya) due to his own inherent merits (mazaya) or to Allah's preference? He states that the latter is the position of the verifiers (ahl al-tahqiq) among the theologians, citing al-Sanusi. Next, he explains the second phrase 'وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلا' (and the best of those who attained the high stations). Here, 'مَنْ' is more general, applying to any human being, not just messengers. This phrase is thus broader than the first, encompassing the Prophet's excellence over all humans, not just prophets. He briefly defines 'العُلَا' as plural of 'عُلْيَا'. Then he notes that the name 'مُحَمَّدٍ' is best read in the nominative case as the predicate of an omitted subject, for glorification. Finally, al-Anbabi adds that the conjunction indicates a refutation of al-Zamakhshari's view that Gabriel is superior to the Prophet, as this phrase asserts the Prophet's supreme rank over all beings.

Key Terms
خير
أفعل تفضيل
مزايا
تفضيل الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Prophet was not a messenger.
D) To emphasize that all prophets are equal.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's superiority is by divine decree, not his own merits, and the grammatical details of the elative and the scope of 'من' support this theological position.

Parsing 'محمد': Badal vs Atf Bayan Conditions
Super-commentary on grammatical parsing of 'محمد'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for valid badal and atf bayan constructions and apply them to the analysis of 'محمد' in al-Bajuri's poem.

Core Idea
Grammatical parsing requires strict adherence to order and definiteness rules.

In this passage, al-Bajuri and al-Anbabiy debate the correct grammatical parsing of the word 'محمد' in a line of poetry. The discussion reveals two key grammatical issues: the ordering of apposition and conjunction, and the agreement in definiteness between apposed elements. Understanding these issues will sharpen your ability to parse Arabic sentences correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proposed grammatical roles
Al-Bajuri states that the prevalent Arabic reading is the genitive, making 'محمد' either a badal (substitute) or عطف بيان (explanatory apposition) for the noun of preference 'خير'. Note the difference: badal replaces without conjunction; عطف بيان explains and requires definiteness agreement.
2
Examine the ordering issue
Al-Anbabiy points out that if 'محمد' is a badal or atf bayan, then the coordinating conjunction 'و' in 'وخير من حاز المقامات' would precede the apposition, which is the reverse of the expected order. He notes that normally the apposition should come before the conjunction. This creates a difficulty.
3
Understand the definiteness condition for عطف بيان
Al-Anbabiy then raises a second issue: عطف بيان requires agreement in definiteness between the apposed and appositive. Since 'خير' is indefinite (because 'من' is indefinite), and 'محمد' is definite, this violates the condition. This is a key grammatical rule from Ibn Malik.
4
Evaluate the proposed solutions
Al-Anbabiy offers two solutions: first, that the conjunction attaches not to 'خير' but to the relative clause 'من حاز المقامات'; second, that if 'من' is interpreted as a relative pronoun, then 'خير' becomes definite by addition, satisfying the condition. He also references al-Zamakhshari's view that permits definite on indefinite in some cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُحَمَّدٍ سَيِّدِ كُلِّ مُقْتَفَى العَرَبِيِّ الهَاشِمِيّ المُصْطَفَى
الباجوري
قَوْلُهُ : (مُحَمَّدٍ) المُنَاسِبُ لِلتَّعْظِيمِ : رَفْعُهُ؛ عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَرٌ لِمُبْتَدَأَ مَحْذُوفٍ، وَالجُمْلَةُ مُسْتَانَفَةٌ كَالجُمْلَةِ السَّابِقَةِ .
وَإِنْ كَانَ الرَّاجِحُ عَرَبِيَّةٌ : الجَرُّ ; بَدَلاً أَوْ عَطْفَ بَيَانٍ) ، لِمُوَافَقَتِهِ لِلأَصْلِ مِنْ عَدَمِ التَّقْدِيرِ؛
الأنبابي
قوله : (بَدَلاً أَوْ عَطْفَ بَيَانٍ يلزمُ على هذا : تقدُّم عطف النسق، وهو قوله : «وَخَيْرُ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتُ العُلا على البدل أو عطف البيان، مع أنَّهما مقدَّمان عليه . والجواب عنه : بأنَّ محلَّ المنع إذا كان المعطوف أجنبياً، وهنا ليس كذلك ؛ إذ خيرُ مَن حاز المقامات هو خير من قد أرسلا غير معلوم في كتب النحو . والجواب بأنَّ محطّ العطف مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتُ العُلا ، لا خير ، فعطفُ النَّسق وكلٌّ مِنَ البدل وعطف البيان لم يتواردا على شيء واحدٍ بعيد، فلعل هناك قولاً بجواز ذلك . نعم؛ إن جعل بدلاً أو عطف بيان من خير الثَّاني لم يلزم ما ذكر؛ إلَّا أنَّه بعيد.
ثمَّ إنَّه يلزم على عطف البيان مخالفته للمعطوف عليه ؛ لأنَّه معرفةٌ، والمعطوف عليه نكرة؛ لأنَّ «مَن» المضاف إليها خير نكرةٌ موصوفةٌ، بدليل أنَّ المحشي أوقعها على نبي أو إنسان، والموافقة في ذلك شرط ؛ كما قال ابن مالك : فَأَوْلِينَهُ مِنْ وِفَاقِ الأَوَّلِ مَا مِنْ وِفَاقِ الأَوَّلِ النَّعْتُ وَلِي فلعل المحشي جرى على رأي الزَّمخشري المجوّز عطف المعرفة عطف بيان على النكرة، فإن جعلت «مَنْ» موصولةً حصلت المطابقة ؛ لأنَّ أفعل التفضيل يتعرَّف بالإضافة.
مُحَمَّدٍ سَيِّدِ كُلِّ مُقْتَفَى العَرَبِيِّ الهَاشِمِيّ المُصْطَفَى. Al-Bajuri: His statement: (مُحَمَّدٍ) – the appropriate for exaltation is its being in the nominative case, as a predicate of an omitted subject, and the sentence is an independent one like the preceding sentence. And although the prevalent in Arabic is the genitive, as a badal or atf bayan, because it conforms to the original without estimation. Al-Anbabiy: His statement: (بَدَلاً أَوْ عَطْفَ بَيَانٍ) – it follows from this that the coordinating conjunction (عطف النسق), which is his statement 'وَخَيْرُ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتُ العُلَا', precedes the badal or atf bayan, even though the latter two are actually placed before it. And the answer is: that the prohibition applies if the conjoined element is foreign, but here it is not; because 'خيرُ مَن حاز المقامات' is not known to be the same as 'خير من قد أرسلا' in the books of grammar. And another answer: that the object of the conjunction is 'مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتُ العُلا', not 'خير', so the coordinating conjunction and each of the badal and atf bayan are not applied to one thing. This is far-fetched, and perhaps there is a view allowing it. Yes, if it is made a badal or atf bayan from the second 'خير', what was mentioned would not follow; but it is far-fetched. Then, there follows upon atf bayan a violation of agreement with the substituted-from, because it is definite, and the substituted-from is indefinite; because 'مَنْ' added to 'خير' is an indefinite described noun, as evidence that the commentator applied it to a prophet or human, and agreement in that is a condition, as Ibn Mālik said: 'Give it from the agreement of the first what the description is given from the agreement of the first'. Perhaps the commentator followed the view of al-Zamakhsharī, who permitted making a definite as an explanatory apposition to an indefinite. If 'مَنْ' is made a relative pronoun, then agreement is achieved, because the noun of preference becomes definite by addition.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage focuses on the grammatical reading of the word 'محمد' in the poem. Al-Bajuri observes that for exaltation, the nominative case (رفع) would be appropriate, making it the predicate of an omitted subject (e.g., 'هو محمد'). However, the more common usage in Arabic is the genitive (جر) as a badal (substitute) or عطف بيان (explanatory apposition). The super-commentator al-Anbabiy then raises a difficulty: if 'محمد' is a badal or atf bayan, it would be preceded by the coordinating conjunction (عطف النسق) 'وخير من حاز المقامات العلا', which logically should come after the apposition, but the apposition is actually the first item in sequence. He presents several attempted solutions: first, that the conjunction is not attached to the main term 'خير' but to the subordinate phrase 'من حاز المقامات العلا'; second, that the prohibition applies only when the conjoined elements are foreign to each other, but here the two phrases are not identical; third, that maybe there is a view allowing such ordering. He also notes the issue of definiteness: عطف البيان requires agreement in definiteness between the appositive and the apposed. Since the original 'خير' is indefinite (because 'من' is indefinite), but 'محمد' is definite, this violates the condition. To resolve this, al-Anbabiy suggests that the commentator might have followed al-Zamakhshari's school, which permits definite on indefinite in this construction, or that if 'من' is considered a relative pronoun, then 'خير' becomes definite by addition to the relative clause, thus satisfying the agreement condition.

Key Terms
بَدَل
عَطْف بَيَان
عَطْف النَّسَق
أَفْعَل التَّفْضِيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Anbabiy, why is it problematic to take 'محمد' as a badal or عطف بيان?
A) Because it violates case agreement.
B) Because the coordinating conjunction precedes the apposition.
C) Because it is not permissible in Arabic grammar.
D) Because it changes the meaning of the poem.

Key Takeaway
The grammatical parsing of 'محمد' in al-Bajuri's poem hinges on resolving ordering and definiteness constraints for badal and atf bayan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Grammatical Analysis of 'Sayyid Kull Muqtafā': Badal and 'Atf Bayān Conditions
Commentator examines the grammatical possibilities and problems for the phrase 'sayyid kull muqtafā'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for badal and 'atf bayān and apply them to resolve a grammatical problem in a Prophetic praise phrase.

Core Idea
Grammatical substitution requires agreement in definiteness and proper ordering.

In this passage, the commentator critically examines whether the phrase 'sayyid kull muqtafā' functions as a badal or 'atf bayān to the Prophet's name. The discussion reveals important grammatical conditions: substitution must not violate ordering of appositives, and explanatory apposition requires definiteness agreement. Understanding these conditions helps us appreciate the precision of classical Arabic grammar in preserving the meaning of sacred texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical problem
The phrase 'sayyid kull muqtafā' is analyzed as badal or 'atf bayān for the noble expression (the Prophet's name). But it appears after 'wa-khayru man ḥāza al-maqāmāt al-‘ulā', which is an 'atf nasaq. Badal or 'atf bayān should precede 'atf nasaq, but here it follows.
2
Understand the ordering issue
The commentator addresses the ordering problem by arguing that the prohibition of delaying a substitute only applies if the conjoined element is foreign to the substitute, which is not the case here because both refer to the same entity.
3
Examine the definiteness condition for 'atf bayān
For 'atf bayān, the conjoined and conjoined-to must agree in definiteness. Here, 'sayyid' (definite by annexation) and 'khayr man qad ursila' (indefinite because 'man' is indefinite) disagree, violating the condition.
4
Find the resolution
The commentator suggests making 'man' a relative pronoun (mawṣūla), which becomes definite by the relative clause. Then the superlative 'khayr' becomes definite by annexation, achieving the required agreement.
This follows al-Zamakhshari's view allowing conjoining a definite as 'atf bayān to an indefinite.
5
Consider the alternative interpretation
If the phrase is made a badal or 'atf bayān from 'khayr' (the second occurrence), the ordering problem is avoided, but the commentator considers this far-fetched.

قوله : (بَدَلاً أَوْ عَطْفَ بَيَانٍ يلزم على هذا : تقدُّم عطف النسق، وهو قوله : «وَخَيْرُ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتُ الْعُلا» على البدل أو عطف البيان، مع أنَّهما مقدَّمان عليه . والجواب عنه : بأنَّ محلَّ المنع إذا كان المعطوف أجنبياً، وهنا ليس كذلك ; إذ خيرُ مَن حاز المقامات هو خير من قد أرسلا غير معلوم في كتب النحو . والجواب بأنَّ محطّ العطف مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتُ الْعُلا ، لا خير , فعطفُ النَّسق وكلٌّ مِنَ البدل وعطف البيان لم يتواردا على شيء واحدٍ بعيد، فلعل هناك قولاً بجواز ذلك . نعم; إن جعل بدلاً أو عطف بيان من خير» الثَّاني لم يلزم ما ذكر; إلَّا أنَّه بعيد.
ثمَّ إنَّه يلزم على عطف البيان مخالفته للمعطوف عليه ; لأنَّه معرفةٌ، والمعطوف عليه نكرة; لأنَّ «مَن» المضاف إليها خير» نكرةٌ موصوفةٌ، بدليل أنَّ المحشي أوقعها على نبي أو إنسان، والموافقة في ذلك شرط ; كما قال ابن مالك : فَأَوْلِيْنَهُ مِنْ وفَاقِ الأَوَّلِ مَا مِنْ وِفَاقِ الأَوَّلِ النَّعْتُ وَلِي فلعل المحشي جرى على رأي الزَّمخشري المجوّز عطف المعرفة عطف بيان على النكرة، فإن جعلت «مَنْ» موصولةً حصلت المطابقة ; لأنَّ أفعل التفضيل يتعرَّف بالإضافة.
وَلَا يَرِدُ : أَنَّ المُبْدَلَ مِنْهُ فِي نِيّة الطَّرْحِ ; لأنَّ التَّحْقِيقَ أَنَّ ذَلِكَ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِعَمَلِ العَامِلِ، أَوْ أَنَّهُ أَمْرٌ أَغْلَبِيٌّ . - وَيُبْعِدُ جَوَازَ النَّصْبِ رَسْمُهُ بِدُونِ أَلِفِ عَلَى مَا هُوَ الشَّائِعُ مِنْ كِتَابَةِ المَنْصُوبِ المُنَوَّنِ بِالأَلِفِ، لَا عَلَى عَادَةِ المُتَقَدِّمِينَ مِنْ كِتَابَتِهِمْ إِيَّاهُ بِصُورَةِ المَرْفُوعِ وَالمَجْرُورٍ; لِاسْتِغْنَائِهِمْ عَنْ رَسْمِ الأَلِفِ بِتَكَرُّرِ الشَّكْلِ , كَذَا نَقَلَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ عَنِ النَّوَوِيِّ وَالسُّيُوطِيِّ، وَفِي كَلَامِ بَعْضِهِمْ : أَنَّ ذَلِكَ طَرِيقَةُ رَبِيعَةَ، وَهُوَ المُوَافِقُ لِلغَتِهِمْ مِنَ الوَقْفِ عَلَيْهِ بِغَيْرِ أَلِفِ. قَوْلُهُ : (سَيّدِ كُلِّ مُقْتَفَى بَدَلٌ أَوْ عَطْفُ بَيَانٍ مِنَ اللَّفْظِ الشَّرِيفِ، وَإِنْ لَزِمَ الإِبْدَالُ مِنَ البَدَلِ عَلَى جَعْلِ اللَّفْظِ الشَّرِيفِ بَدَلاً , وَالجُمْهُورُ لَا يُجِيرُونَهُ. وَلَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ نَعْتاً ; لأَنَّهُ نَكِرَةٌ، وَاللَّفْظُ الشَّرِيفُ مَعْرِفَةٌ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ وَصْفُ المَعْرِفَةِ بِالنَّكِرَةِ .
He said: (As a badal or 'atf bayān) It follows from this the precedence of 'atf al-nasaq, which is his statement 'And the best of those who attained the highest stations' over the badal or 'atf bayān, even though both are preceded by it. The answer to this: that the place of prohibition is when the conjoined is foreign, and here it is not so. For 'the best of those who attained the stations' is 'the best of those who were sent' unknown in grammar books. And the answer: that the locus of the conjunction is 'who attained the highest stations', not 'the best', so 'atf al-nasaq and each of badal and 'atf bayān did not apply to one thing; it is far-fetched. Perhaps there is a saying permitting that. Yes; if it is made a badal or 'atf bayān from 'the best' the second, what was mentioned does not follow; except that it is far-fetched. Then it follows from 'atf bayān its contradiction of the conjoined-to because it is definite, and the conjoined-to is indefinite; because 'man' added to 'khayr' is an indefinite described, evidenced by the commentator applying it to a prophet or a human, and agreement in that is a condition, as Ibn Malik said: 'So give it from agreement with the first. What from agreement with the first, the attribute follows.' Perhaps the commentator followed the opinion of al-Zamakhshari who permitted conjoining a definite as 'atf bayān to an indefinite. If 'man' is made a relative pronoun, agreement is achieved because the superlative becomes definite by annexation. And it is not objected: that the substituted-from is in intention of dropping, because the researched is that that is relative to the operation of the operator, or that it is a common matter. And it is far-fetched to allow the accusative, its drawing without an alif according to what is common from writing the accusative nunated with alif, not according to the custom of the predecessors of writing it in the form of the nominative and genitive; because they were independent of drawing the alif by repeating the diacritic. Thus some transmitted it from al-Nawawi and al-Suyuti. And in the speech of some: that that is the method of Rabi'a, and it is agreeing with their language of stopping upon it without alif. His statement: (Sayyid kull muqtafā is a badal or an 'atf bayān from the noble expression, even if substitution from the badal follows upon making the noble expression a badal, and the majority do not allow it. And it is not correct to be an attribute because it is indefinite, and the noble expression is definite, and description of the definite by the indefinite is not permitted.)
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical commentary (hāshiya) that critically refines the analysis of a phrase praising the Prophet, specifically 'sayyid kull muqtafā' (leader of every follower). The commentator addresses whether this phrase functions as a badal (substitute) or 'atf bayān (explanatory apposition) to the preceding word 'Muhammad' or to 'khayr man qad ursila' (best of those who were sent). The discussion begins with a problem: the phrase appears after 'wa-khayru man ḥāza al-maqāmāt al-‘ulā' (and the best of those who attained the highest stations), which is itself an 'atf nasaq (sequential conjunction) of the preceding. If 'sayyid kull muqtafā' is a badal or 'atf bayān, it should have preceded the 'atf nasaq, but it does not. Two answers are given: first, the prohibition of delaying a substitute only applies if the conjoined element is foreign to the substitute, which is not the case here because both refer to the same entity. Second, the locus of the conjunction is the phrase 'man ḥāza al-maqāmāt al-‘ulā', not 'khayr', so there is no conflict. Then the commentator notes that if instead the phrase is made a badal or 'atf bayān from 'khayr' (the second one, meaning the second occurrence of 'khayr'), the problem is avoided, though this is far-fetched. Next, he raises a specific issue with 'atf bayān: it requires agreement in definiteness between the conjoined elements. The conjoined word 'sayyid' is definite (by annexation to 'kull muqtafā'), but the conjoined-to ('khayr man qad ursila') is indefinite because 'man' is an indefinite relative pronoun. To resolve this, the commentator suggests making 'man' a relative pronoun (mawṣūla), which becomes definite by the relative clause; then the superlative 'af‘al al-tafḍīl' (khayr) becomes definite by annexation. This follows al-Zamakhshari's view allowing conjoining a definite as 'atf bayān to an indefinite. Then he dismisses the objection that the substituted-from (mubdal minhu) is in the intention of dropping (like an appositive), because that rule applies only to the operation of the operator (the grammatical agent governing the substitute), not to the substitute itself, or it is a common (probable) matter. Finally, the commentator discusses the writing of the nunation: the word 'sayyid' if read in the accusative would normally be written with an alif (e.g., 'sayyidan'), but in the text it is written without alif, which is the practice of the early Arabs who relied on diacritics, and also the method of Rabī‘a. The passage ends by reaffirming that 'sayyid kull muqtafā' is a badal or 'atf bayān from the noble expression (the name of the Prophet), even though this would require substitution from a substitute (badal min al-badal), which the majority does not permit; however, it cannot be an attribute (na‘t) because it is indefinite and the described is definite.

Commentary Notes
intermediate
8 min
Grammar of Apposition in Praising the Prophet
Grammatical analysis of 'sayyid kulli muqtafa' as badal not na't.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between badal (apposition) and na't (adjective) in the context of describing the Prophet, and identify the grammatical rule that prevents using an indefinite adjective for a definite noun.

Core Idea
An indefinite cannot describe a definite; apposition solves the grammatical conflict.

When poets praise the Prophet, they often use phrases like 'sayyid kulli muqtafa' after his name. Is this an adjective (na't) or an apposition (badal)? The author of this commentary clarifies that it must be badal, because an indefinite adjective cannot describe a definite noun. Understanding this rule helps you parse classical praise poetry correctly and appreciate the precision of Arabic grammar in theological contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms involved
Look at the phrase 'sayyid kulli muqtafa' and the preceding noun 'Muhammad'. Note that 'Muhammad' is definite (proper noun) while 'sayyid kulli muqtafa' is indefinite (lacking alif lam).
In Arabic, proper names are definite even without the article.
2
Check the grammatical compatibility
Recall the rule: adjectives (na't) must agree with the noun they describe in definiteness. Since 'sayyid' is indefinite, it cannot be an adjective for a definite noun.
This is a basic rule of Arabic grammar.
3
Consider alternative roles
If not na't, the phrase can be badal (apposition) or 'atf bayan (explanatory conjunction). The author confirms that both are permissible, but badal is preferred because it allows the indefinite to replace the definite in grammatical function.
The author also notes that if you make the noble name itself a badal, it leads to substitution from a badal, which the majority reject.
4
Apply to the poem's spelling
Notice that the word 'Muhammad' is written without an alif in the accusative case. This early Arab practice dispensed with the alif by relying on shape repetition, as transmitted from al-Nawawi and al-Suyuti.
This shows that grammatical rules must also consider historical scribal conventions.
5
Draw the lesson
From this analysis, you learn that when you see an indefinite phrase following a definite noun in praise texts, it is likely a badal, not an adjective. This protects you from misreading the grammar of classical Islamic poetry.
