مُحَمَّدٍ سَيِّدِ كُلِّ مُقْتَفَى العَرَبِيِّ الهَاشِمِيِّ المُصْطَفَى. وَلَا يَرِدُ : أَنَّ المُبْدَلَ مِنْهُ فِي نِيّة الطَّرْحِ؛ لأنَّ التَّحْقِيقَ أَنَّ ذَلِكَ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِعَمَلِ العَامِلِ، أَوْ أَنَّهُ أَمْرٌ أَغْلَبِيٌّ . - وَيُبْعِدُ جَوَازَ النَّصْبِ رَسْمُهُ بِدُونِ أَلِفِ عَلَى مَا هُوَ الشَّائِعُ مِنْ كِتَابَةِ المَنْصُوبِ المُنَوَّنِ بِالأَلِفِ، لَا عَلَى عَادَةِ المُتَقَدِّمِينَ مِنْ كِتَابَتِهِمْ إِيَّاهُ بِصُورَةِ المَرْفُوعِ وَالمَجْرُورٍ؛ لِاسْتِغْنَائِهِمْ عَنْ رَسْمِ الأَلِفِ بِتَكَرُّرِ الشَّكْلِ، كَذَا نَقَلَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ عَنِ النَّوَوِيِّ وَالسُّيُوطِيِّ، وَفِي كَلَامِ بَعْضِهِمْ : أَنَّ ذَلِكَ طَرِيقَةُ رَبِيعَةَ، وَهُوَ المُوَافِقُ لِلغَتِهِمْ مِنَ الوَقْفِ عَلَيْهِ بِغَيْرِ أَلِفِ. قَوْلُهُ : (سَيّدِ كُلِّ مُقْتَفَى بَدَلٌ أَوْ عَطْفُ بَيَانٍ مِنَ اللَّفْظِ الشَّرِيفِ، وَإِنْ لَزِمَ الإِبْدَالُ مِنَ البَدَلِ عَلَى جَعْلِ اللَّفْظِ الشَّرِيفِ بَدَلاً، وَالجُمْهُورُ لَا يُجِيرُونَهُ. وَلَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ نَعْتاً؛ لأَنَّهُ نَكِرَةٌ، وَاللَّفْظُ الشَّرِيفُ مَعْرِفَةٌ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ وَصْفُ المَعْرِفَةِ بِالنَّكِرَةِ. وَالمُقْتَفَى : المُتَّبَعُ، وَهُوَ : الرَّسُولُ، فَكَأَنَّهُ قَالَ: «سَيِّدُ كُلِّ رَسُولٍ». وَإِطْلَاقُ السَّيِّدِ عَلَيْهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مَأخوذُ مِنْ حَدِيثِ: «أَنَا سَيِّدُ وَلَدِ آدَمَ يَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ وَلَا فَخْرُ». وَالمُرَادُ مِنْ وَلَدِ آدَمَ - كَمَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ - : النَّوعُ الإِنْسَانِيُّ، فَهُوَ شَامِلٌ لِآدَمَ أَيْضاً، وَبِذَلِكَ انْدَفَعَ مَا قَدْ يُقَالُ: هَذَا الحَدِيثُ لَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى سِيَادَتِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَلَى آدَمَ، وَإِنَّمَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى سِيَادَتِهِ عَلَى أَوْلَادِهِ فَقَط. وَدَفَعَ بَعْضُهُمْ ذَلِكَ أَيْضاً : بِأَنَّ فِي أَوْلَادِ آدَمَ مَنْ هُمْ أَفْضَلُ مِنْهُ كَـ: «إِبْرَاهِيمَ، وَمُوسَى وَعِيْسَى عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ، وَإِذَا كَانَ صلى الله عليه وسلم سَيِّدُ الأَفْضَلِ، كَانَ سَيِّدَ المَفْضُولِ بِالطَّرِيقِ الأَوْلَى. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: قَدْ وَرَدَ أَنَّهُ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «السَّيِّدُ الله»، وَهُوَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَا يُطْلَقُ «السَّيِّدُ» عَلَى غَيْرِهِ تَعَالَى. أُجِيبَ : بِأَنَّهُ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى السِّيَادَةِ المُطْلَقَةِ. قَوْلُهُ : (العَرَبِيُّ) أَي : المَنْسُوبِ لِلعَرَبِ. وَقَوْلُهُ : (الهَاشِمِيُّ) أي : المَنْسُوبِ لِهَاشِمٍ؛ لأَنَّهُ مِنْ ذُرِيَّتِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ وَ ابْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبْدِ المُطَّلِبِ بْنِ هَاشِمٍ - الَّذِي هُوَ أَخُو المُطَّلِبِ؛ الَّذِي مِنْ ذُرِّيَّتِهِ الإِمَامُ الشَّافِعِيُّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُ، فَلِذَلِكَ يُقَالُ لَهُ : الْمُطَّلِبِيُّ نِسْبَةً لِلمُطَّلِبِ.
Muhammad, the leader of every followed one, the Arab, the Hashimi, the Chosen. And it is not objected that the substituted from is in the intention of dropping; because the verification is that that is with respect to the operation of the operator, or that it is a prevalent matter. And it distances the permissibility of the accusative case drawing it without an alif according to what is common from writing the accusative nunated with an alif, not upon the custom of the early ones from writing it in the form of the nominative and genitive; because they dispensed with drawing the alif by the repetition of the shape, thus some of them transmitted it from al-Nawawi and al-Suyuti. And in the speech of some of them: that that is the way of Rabi'a, and it is in agreement with their language of stopping upon it without an alif. His statement: (Sayyid kulli muqtafa) is a badal or an explanatory conjunction from the noble expression, even if substitution from a badal follows if the noble expression is made a badal, and the majority do not permit it. And it is not correct that it be a na'at; because it is indefinite, and the noble expression is definite, and it is not permissible to describe the definite with the indefinite. And al-muqtafa: the followed, and it is the messenger, so it is as if he said: 'Leader of every messenger.' And the usage of 'sayyid' for him, peace be upon him, is taken from the hadith: 'I am the leader of the children of Adam on the Day of Judgement and no boast.' And what is intended by children of Adam—as some of them said—is the human species, so it is inclusive of Adam also, and by that is repelled what might be said: This hadith does not indicate his leadership over Adam, but rather indicates his leadership over his children only. And some of them repelled that also: by saying that among the children of Adam are those who are better than him, such as Abraham, Moses, and Jesus, peace be upon them, and if he is the leader of the best, then he is the leader of the lesser by the primary way. For if it is said: It has been reported that he, peace be upon him, said: 'God is the Lord (sayyid),' and that indicates that 'sayyid' is not applied to other than Him, Exalted. It is answered: That it is construed upon absolute lordship. His statement: (al-'Arabiyy) meaning: the one ascribed to the Arabs. And his statement: (al-Hashimiyy) meaning: the one ascribed to Hashim; because he is from his descendants, for he is the son of Abdullah ibn Abd al-Muttalib ibn Hashim—who is the brother of al-Muttalib; from whose descendants is Imam al-Shafi'i, may God be pleased with him. Therefore he is called al-Muttalibi in lineage to al-Muttalib.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening line of the poem, which praises the Prophet Muhammad with attributes: 'Leader of every followed one, the Arab, the Hashimi, the Chosen.' The author first addresses a grammatical issue: the phrase 'sayyid kulli muqtafa' is in apposition (badal) or explanatory conjunction ('atf bayan) to the preceding noble name 'Muhammad', not an adjective (na't), because it is indefinite while the name is definite. He then discusses the spelling of the accusative case without alif, citing scholars like al-Nawawi and al-Suyuti, and the practice of the early Arabs who relied on shape repetition. The author defines 'muqtafa' as 'the followed', i.e., the Messenger, making the phrase equivalent to 'Leader of every messenger'. He then defends the use of 'sayyid' for the Prophet by referencing the famous hadith 'I am the leader of the children of Adam', explaining that 'children of Adam' means the human species, thus including Adam himself. Some objected that the hadith only covers Adam's offspring, but the author counters that among those offspring are prophets better than Adam (like Abraham, Moses, Jesus), and being leader of the best implies leadership of the lesser a fortiori. Another objection is raised from the hadith 'God is the sayyid', which might restrict the title to God alone. The answer is that this hadith refers to absolute lordship, not the relative leadership attributed to the Prophet. Finally, he explains the attributes 'al-'Arabiyy' (the Arab) and 'al-Hashimiyy' (the Hashimi), noting the Prophet's lineage to Hashim and the connection to Imam al-Shafi'i through al-Muttalib.

Checkpoint
Why cannot 'sayyid kulli muqtafa' be an adjective (na't) for 'Muhammad'?
A) Because adjectives must follow the noun directly.
B) Because the phrase is too long to be an adjective.
C) Because 'sayyid kulli muqtafa' is indefinite and 'Muhammad' is definite.
D) Because the poet intended it as an apposition.

Key Takeaway
An indefinite phrase cannot serve as an adjective for a definite noun in Arabic; apposition (badal) resolves this in prophetic praise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a line from a praise poem of the Prophet (e.g., al-Burda or Qasidat al-Burda) where an indefinite phrase follows a definite noun. Determine whether it is a na't, badal, or other construction based on the definiteness rule.
?

Defending the Title 'Sayyid' for the Prophet
Theological defense of calling the Prophet 'sayyid' using hadith and logical responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute theological objections against calling the Prophet 'sayyid' (leader) by using the hadith 'I am the leader of the children of Adam' and the distinction between absolute and relative lordship.

Core Idea
The Prophet is sayyid over all creation, including Adam, by a fortiori logic and sound hadith interpretation.

Calling the Prophet 'sayyid' (leader) is common in Islamic praise, but some object based on a hadith that says 'God is the sayyid' (السيد الله). Others argue that the hadith 'I am the leader of the children of Adam' excludes Adam himself. In this passage, the author systematically refutes both objections, showing that the Prophet is indeed the leader of all humanity, including Adam, and that the divine title refers to absolute lordship, not relative leadership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first objection
The first objection: the hadith 'I am the leader of the children of Adam' only covers Adam's offspring, not Adam himself, because Adam is the father.
This is a literal reading of 'children of Adam'.
2
Analyze the author's response to the first objection
The author counters that 'children of Adam' means the human species, which includes Adam. He supports this by noting that among Adam's children are prophets better than Adam (Abraham, Moses, Jesus), and if the Prophet is their leader, he is necessarily Adam's leader as well, a fortiori.
This uses an argument from the better to the lesser (طريق الأولى).
3
Identify the second objection
The second objection: the hadith 'السيد الله' (God is the Sayyid) seems to prohibit calling anyone else 'sayyid'.
This is a stronger theological objection.
4
Analyze the author's response to the second objection
The author explains that the hadith refers to absolute lordship (السيادة المطلقة), which belongs only to God, not the relative leadership (السيادة النسبية) attributed to the Prophet. Thus, there is no contradiction.
This distinction allows using 'sayyid' for the Prophet in a limited sense.
5
Draw the lesson
You now see how careful interpretation of hadith and logical reasoning (a fortiori) defends the honorifics of the Prophet. The same method can be applied to other apparent conflicts between texts.

Source Text

مُحَمَّدٍ سَيِّدِ كُلِّ مُقْتَفَى العَرَبِيِّ الهَاشِمِيِّ المُصْطَفَى. وَلَا يَرِدُ : أَنَّ المُبْدَلَ مِنْهُ فِي نِيّة الطَّرْحِ؛ لأنَّ التَّحْقِيقَ أَنَّ ذَلِكَ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِعَمَلِ العَامِلِ، أَوْ أَنَّهُ أَمْرٌ أَغْلَبِيٌّ . - وَيُبْعِدُ جَوَازَ النَّصْبِ رَسْمُهُ بِدُونِ أَلِفِ عَلَى مَا هُوَ الشَّائِعُ مِنْ كِتَابَةِ المَنْصُوبِ المُنَوَّنِ بِالأَلِفِ، لَا عَلَى عَادَةِ المُتَقَدِّمِينَ مِنْ كِتَابَتِهِمْ إِيَّاهُ بِصُورَةِ المَرْفُوعِ وَالمَجْرُورٍ؛ لِاسْتِغْنَائِهِمْ عَنْ رَسْمِ الأَلِفِ بِتَكَرُّرِ الشَّكْلِ، كَذَا نَقَلَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ عَنِ النَّوَوِيِّ وَالسُّيُوطِيِّ، وَفِي كَلَامِ بَعْضِهِمْ : أَنَّ ذَلِكَ طَرِيقَةُ رَبِيعَةَ، وَهُوَ المُوَافِقُ لِلغَتِهِمْ مِنَ الوَقْفِ عَلَيْهِ بِغَيْرِ أَلِفِ. قَوْلُهُ : (سَيّدِ كُلِّ مُقْتَفَى بَدَلٌ أَوْ عَطْفُ بَيَانٍ مِنَ اللَّفْظِ الشَّرِيفِ، وَإِنْ لَزِمَ الإِبْدَالُ مِنَ البَدَلِ عَلَى جَعْلِ اللَّفْظِ الشَّرِيفِ بَدَلاً، وَالجُمْهُورُ لَا يُجِيرُونَهُ. وَلَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ نَعْتاً؛ لأَنَّهُ نَكِرَةٌ، وَاللَّفْظُ الشَّرِيفُ مَعْرِفَةٌ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ وَصْفُ المَعْرِفَةِ بِالنَّكِرَةِ. وَالمُقْتَفَى : المُتَّبَعُ، وَهُوَ : الرَّسُولُ، فَكَأَنَّهُ قَالَ: «سَيِّدُ كُلِّ رَسُولٍ». وَإِطْلَاقُ السَّيِّدِ عَلَيْهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مَأخوذُ مِنْ حَدِيثِ: «أَنَا سَيِّدُ وَلَدِ آدَمَ يَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ وَلَا فَخْرُ». وَالمُرَادُ مِنْ وَلَدِ آدَمَ - كَمَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ - : النَّوعُ الإِنْسَانِيُّ، فَهُوَ شَامِلٌ لِآدَمَ أَيْضاً، وَبِذَلِكَ انْدَفَعَ مَا قَدْ يُقَالُ: هَذَا الحَدِيثُ لَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى سِيَادَتِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَلَى آدَمَ، وَإِنَّمَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى سِيَادَتِهِ عَلَى أَوْلَادِهِ فَقَط. وَدَفَعَ بَعْضُهُمْ ذَلِكَ أَيْضاً : بِأَنَّ فِي أَوْلَادِ آدَمَ مَنْ هُمْ أَفْضَلُ مِنْهُ كَـ: «إِبْرَاهِيمَ، وَمُوسَى وَعِيْسَى عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ، وَإِذَا كَانَ صلى الله عليه وسلم سَيِّدُ الأَفْضَلِ، كَانَ سَيِّدَ المَفْضُولِ بِالطَّرِيقِ الأَوْلَى. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: قَدْ وَرَدَ أَنَّهُ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «السَّيِّدُ الله»، وَهُوَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَا يُطْلَقُ «السَّيِّدُ» عَلَى غَيْرِهِ تَعَالَى. أُجِيبَ : بِأَنَّهُ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى السِّيَادَةِ المُطْلَقَةِ. قَوْلُهُ : (العَرَبِيُّ) أَي : المَنْسُوبِ لِلعَرَبِ. وَقَوْلُهُ : (الهَاشِمِيُّ) أي : المَنْسُوبِ لِهَاشِمٍ؛ لأَنَّهُ مِنْ ذُرِيَّتِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ وَ ابْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبْدِ المُطَّلِبِ بْنِ هَاشِمٍ - الَّذِي هُوَ أَخُو المُطَّلِبِ؛ الَّذِي مِنْ ذُرِّيَّتِهِ الإِمَامُ الشَّافِعِيُّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُ، فَلِذَلِكَ يُقَالُ لَهُ : الْمُطَّلِبِيُّ نِسْبَةً لِلمُطَّلِبِ.
Muhammad, the leader of every followed one, the Arab, the Hashimi, the Chosen. And it is not objected that the substituted from is in the intention of dropping; because the verification is that that is with respect to the operation of the operator, or that it is a prevalent matter. And it distances the permissibility of the accusative case drawing it without an alif according to what is common from writing the accusative nunated with an alif, not upon the custom of the early ones from writing it in the form of the nominative and genitive; because they dispensed with drawing the alif by the repetition of the shape, thus some of them transmitted it from al-Nawawi and al-Suyuti. And in the speech of some of them: that that is the way of Rabi'a, and it is in agreement with their language of stopping upon it without an alif. His statement: (Sayyid kulli muqtafa) is a badal or an explanatory conjunction from the noble expression, even if substitution from a badal follows if the noble expression is made a badal, and the majority do not permit it. And it is not correct that it be a na'at; because it is indefinite, and the noble expression is definite, and it is not permissible to describe the definite with the indefinite. And al-muqtafa: the followed, and it is the messenger, so it is as if he said: 'Leader of every messenger.' And the usage of 'sayyid' for him, peace be upon him, is taken from the hadith: 'I am the leader of the children of Adam on the Day of Judgement and no boast.' And what is intended by children of Adam—as some of them said—is the human species, so it is inclusive of Adam also, and by that is repelled what might be said: This hadith does not indicate his leadership over Adam, but rather indicates his leadership over his children only. And some of them repelled that also: by saying that among the children of Adam are those who are better than him, such as Abraham, Moses, and Jesus, peace be upon them, and if he is the leader of the best, then he is the leader of the lesser by the primary way. For if it is said: It has been reported that he, peace be upon him, said: 'God is the Lord (sayyid),' and that indicates that 'sayyid' is not applied to other than Him, Exalted. It is answered: That it is construed upon absolute lordship. His statement: (al-'Arabiyy) meaning: the one ascribed to the Arabs. And his statement: (al-Hashimiyy) meaning: the one ascribed to Hashim; because he is from his descendants, for he is the son of Abdullah ibn Abd al-Muttalib ibn Hashim—who is the brother of al-Muttalib; from whose descendants is Imam al-Shafi'i, may God be pleased with him. Therefore he is called al-Muttalibi in lineage to al-Muttalib.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening line of the poem, which praises the Prophet Muhammad with attributes: 'Leader of every followed one, the Arab, the Hashimi, the Chosen.' The author first addresses a grammatical issue: the phrase 'sayyid kulli muqtafa' is in apposition (badal) or explanatory conjunction ('atf bayan) to the preceding noble name 'Muhammad', not an adjective (na't), because it is indefinite while the name is definite. He then discusses the spelling of the accusative case without alif, citing scholars like al-Nawawi and al-Suyuti, and the practice of the early Arabs who relied on shape repetition. The author defines 'muqtafa' as 'the followed', i.e., the Messenger, making the phrase equivalent to 'Leader of every messenger'. He then defends the use of 'sayyid' for the Prophet by referencing the famous hadith 'I am the leader of the children of Adam', explaining that 'children of Adam' means the human species, thus including Adam himself. Some objected that the hadith only covers Adam's offspring, but the author counters that among those offspring are prophets better than Adam (like Abraham, Moses, Jesus), and being leader of the best implies leadership of the lesser a fortiori. Another objection is raised from the hadith 'God is the sayyid', which might restrict the title to God alone. The answer is that this hadith refers to absolute lordship, not the relative leadership attributed to the Prophet. Finally, he explains the attributes 'al-'Arabiyy' (the Arab) and 'al-Hashimiyy' (the Hashimi), noting the Prophet's lineage to Hashim and the connection to Imam al-Shafi'i through al-Muttalib.

Key Terms
سَيِّد
وَلَد آدَم
السَّيَادَة المُطْلَقَة
الطَّرِيق الأَوْلَى

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does the author defend the Prophet's leadership over Adam despite the hadith 'I am the leader of the children of Adam' seemingly excluding Adam?
A) He argues that 'children of Adam' means the human species, which includes Adam.
B) He says the hadith is weak and cannot be used as evidence.
C) He claims Adam is not included because he is the father, not a child.
D) He reinterprets 'leadership' as only spiritual, not hierarchical.

Key Takeaway
The title 'sayyid' for the Prophet is scripturally and logically sound when understood as relative leadership, distinct from God's absolute lordship.

Find another hadith that seems to limit a title to God (e.g., 'None is called al-Hakam but Allah') and explain how scholars distinguish between absolute and relative application, similar to the 'sayyid' case.

Using the a fortiori argument (طريق الأولى), construct a defense for the Prophet's superiority over all prophets, citing the hadith 'أنا سيد ولد آدم' and the fact that he is the leader of prophets better than Adam.

Ordering General Before Specific Attributes
Commentator explains the logical principle of ordering general before specific attributes in descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of ordering general before specific in Arabic descriptive phrases and identify when a departure is justified.

Core Idea
Mentioning the specific after the general adds benefit; the reverse is pointless.

In Arabic rhetoric and logic, the order of attributes matters. The commentator uses the example 'al-Arabi al-Hashimi' and the phrase 'learned researcher' to illustrate that the general should precede the specific for clarity and benefit. This lesson unpacks that principle and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general and specific attributes
In the phrase 'al-Arabi al-Hashimi', 'al-Arabi' is general (all Arabs) and 'al-Hashimi' is specific (descendants of Hashim). Notice which comes first.
2
Recognize the claimed benefit
The commentator states that mentioning the specific after the general has a benefit (it adds specification), while the reverse lacks benefit. Think of the example: 'a learned researcher' clarifies that the researcher is learned, whereas 'a researcher learned' is awkward.
The benefit is that the specific attribute narrows down the general one.
3
Detect the potential objection
The Qur'anic verse 'He was a messenger, a prophet' (Maryam 51) places the general 'messenger' before the specific 'prophet'. This seems to contradict the principle. Note it as a counterexample.
4
Understand the resolution
The commentator explains that the word 'prophet' is in the accusative as a circumstantial accusative (hal), which implies concomitance. Thus, the order is justified because the later word adds the meaning of simultaneous prophethood, not mere succession. This shows an exception when the specific term provides additional information beyond specification.
The hal shows that his messengership was accompanied by prophethood from the start.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (العَرَبِيُّ) أي : المَنْسُوبِ لِلعَرَبِ . وَقَوْلُهُ : (الهَاشِمِيٌّ) أي : المَنْسُوبِ لِهَاشِمٍ؛ لأَنَّهُ مِنْ ذُرِيَّتِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ وَ ابْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبْدِ المُطَّلِبِ بْنِ هَاشِمٍ - الَّذِي هُوَ أَخُو المُطَّلِبِ؛ الَّذِي مِنْ ذُرِّيَّتِهِ الإِمَامُ الشَّافِعِيُّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُ ، فَلِذَلِكَ يُقَالُ لَهُ : الْمُطَّلِبِيُّ نِسْبَةً لِلمُطَّلِبِ . وَلَا يَخْفَى مَا فِي تَقْدِيمِ العَرَبِيّ» عَلَى الهَاشِمِيٌّ مِنْ حُسْنِ التَّرْتِيبِ؛ لِأَنَّ ذِكْرَ الخَاصٌ بَعْدَ العَام لَهُ فَائِدَةٌ، بِخِلَافِ عَكْسِهِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا فَائِدَةَ لَهُ، وَلِذَلِكَ يَقُولُونَ : عَالِمٌ نَحْرِيرٌ وَلَا يَقُولُونَ : نَحْرِيرٌ عَالِمٌ». وَلَا يَرِدُ قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَكَانَ رَسُولًا نَبِيَّا [مريم : ٥١]؛ لِأَنَّهُ وَإِنْ ذُكِرَ فِيهِ العَامُ بَعْدَ الخَاصٌ ، لَكِنَّهُ قَدْ أَفَادَ مُقَارَنَةَ نُبُوَّتِهِ لِرِسَالَتِهِ بِوَاسِطَةِ أَنَّ نَبِيًّا حَالٌ، وَهِيَ تُفِيدُ المُقَارَنَةَ لِعَامِلِهَا .
His statement: 'al-Arabi' means the one attributed to the Arabs. And his statement: 'al-Hashimi' means the one attributed to Hashim, because he is from his progeny; indeed, he is the son of Abdullah bin Abdul-Muttalib bin Hashim, who is the brother of al-Muttalib, from whose progeny is Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him; therefore he is called al-Muttalibi in attribution to al-Muttalib. And it is not hidden what good order there is in placing 'al-Arabi' before 'al-Hashimi', because mentioning the specific after the general has a benefit, unlike the reverse, for there is no benefit in it; and therefore they say: 'a learned researcher' and they do not say: 'a researcher learned'. And His statement, the Exalted, does not refute this: 'And he was a messenger, a prophet' [Maryam 51]; because even though the general is mentioned after the specific in it, yet it has benefited the concomitance of his prophethood to his messengership by virtue of the fact that 'prophet' is a circumstantial accusative (hal), and a circumstantial accusative indicates concomitance to its operative.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on al-Sullam al-Murawnaq, discussing the attributes of the Prophet in the opening line. The commentator first explains the meanings of 'al-Arabi' and 'al-Hashimi', noting the genealogical connection to Hashim and al-Muttalib. Then he draws attention to the order of these attributes: 'al-Arabi' (general) precedes 'al-Hashimi' (specific). He states that this order is good because placing the specific after the general has a benefit (it adds specification), whereas the reverse (the general after the specific) would be pointless—he gives the example: one says 'a learned researcher' not 'a researcher learned'. However, a potential objection arises from the Qur'anic verse "وَكَانَ رَسُولًا نَبِيًّا" where 'rasulan' (general) comes after 'nabiyyan' (specific). The commentator refutes this by explaining that here the word 'nabiyyan' is in the accusative as a circumstantial accusative (hal), and the hal indicates concomitance (muqarana) to its operative. Thus, the verse means that his messengership was in a state of prophethood, which implies that prophethood and messengership were simultaneous from the beginning. So the order is justified by the additional benefit of showing concomitance, which is a valid reason for departing from the usual rule. This discussion illustrates a principle of Arabic rhetorical style that has implications for logical ordering of predicates.

Key Terms
العربي
الهاشمي
الخاص
العام
الحال

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is 'al-Arabi' placed before 'al-Hashimi' in the opening line?
A) Because 'al-Arabi' is more honorable than 'al-Hashimi'.
B) Because mentioning the specific after the general has a benefit.
C) Because it is a poetic necessity.
D) Because it was revealed in the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
In Arabic descriptions, the general attribute should precede the specific unless the specific term provides additional meaning like concomitance, as in the Qur'anic hal construction.

Given the descriptive phrase 'a faqih mujtahid', determine if the order follows the general-before-specific principle and explain why, using the commentator's rationale.
?

The Waw of Conjunction: Verbal vs. Actual in the Salawat Command
Author critiques the poet for separating salawat from taslim and rebuts the proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between waw for verbal conjunction (al-qiran al-dhikri) and waw for actual conjunction (al-qiran al-fi'li) in Quranic commands, and apply this distinction to evaluate arguments about combined acts of worship.

Core Idea
The waw in a command does not always imply simultaneous performance; it may merely join the mention.

In this passage, the commentator critiques a poet for separating salawat from taslim. The poet's opponents used the Quranic verse 'Send blessings upon him and greet him' as a proof that the two must be joined. However, the commentator shows that the waw in the verse is for verbal conjunction only, using the analogy of 'establish prayer and give zakat.' This is a key tool in usul al-fiqh for interpreting commands, helping us avoid overburdening and misunderstanding the nature of combined obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and its proof
The later scholars claim that separating salawat from taslim is disliked. They cite Quran 33:56, where 'sallu' and 'sallimu' are connected by 'waw', as proof that the two must be performed together.
2
Locate the rebuttal
The commentator argues that the waw in that verse is for verbal conjunction (qiran dhikri) not actual conjunction (qiran fi'li). This means the waw joins the mention of the two acts, not that they must be done simultaneously.
This distinction is rooted in usul al-fiqh.
3
Examine the analogy
He compares it to Quran 2:110, 'And establish prayer and give zakat,' where the waw connects the two commands but they are independent obligations without requiring joint performance.
This analogy strengthens the rebuttal by showing a clear precedent.
4
Note the outcome
Based on this, some early scholars did not consider separating salawat from taslim as disliked. However, the commentator adds that it is still contrary to the better practice (khilaf al-awla).
The refinement here is nuanced: not a ruling of prohibition, but a matter of preference.
5
Apply the distinction
Now you can test other Quranic commands with waw to decide whether the conjunction implies joint action or just joint mention. For example, consider Quran 2:43: 'And establish prayer and give zakat.' Does the waw require performing them at the same time?
Use the principle: if the two acts are separate obligations known from other evidence, the waw is likely verbal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَلَى المُصَنِّفِ مُؤَاخَذَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ قَدْ أَفْرَدَ الصَّلَاةَ عَنِ السَّلَامِ وَهُوَ مَكْرُوهُ كَعَكْسِهِ؛ إِلَّا فِيمَا وَرَدَ عَلَى طَرِيقَةِ المُتَاخِرِينَ، وَاسْتَدَلُّوا عَلَى ذَلِكَ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى : يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمُوا تسليمًا [الأحزاب: ٥٦] حَيْثُ قَرَنَ بَيْنَهُمَا بِـ «الوَاوِ . وَرُدَّ هَذَا الاِسْتِدْلَالُ بِأَنَّ الوَاوَ إِنَّمَا هِيَ لِلقِرَانِ الذِّكْرِي دُونَ القِرانِ الفِعْلِي، كَمَا فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلَوٰةَ وَاتُوا الزَّكَوةَ ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۱۰] ، وَلِذَلِكَ رَبَّحَ بَعْضُهُمْ طَرِيقَةَ المُتَقَدِّمِينَ مِنْ عَدَم كَرَاهَةِ ذَلِكَ. نَعَمْ؛ هُوَ خِلَافُ الأَوْلَى قَطعاً . وَالأَحَادِيثُ فِي فَضْل الصَّلَاةِ عَلَيْهِ جَمَّةٌ لَا تَنْضَبِطُ، وَخَصَائِصُهَا لَا تَنْحَصِرُ : - فَمِنْ ذَلِكَ : قَضَاءُ الحَاجَاتِ، وَكَشْفُ الكُرَبِ المُعْضَلَاتِ، وَنُزُولُ الرَّحَمَاتِ. - وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ أَيْضاً : مَا جُرِّبَ مِنْ تَأثِيرِهَا فِي تَنْوِيرِ القُلُوبِ حَتَّى قِيلَ: إِنَّهَا تَكْفِي عَنِ الشَّيْخ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَتَقُومُ مُقَامَهُ، كَمَا حَكَاهُ سَيِّدِي أَحْمَد زَرُّوق وَالشَّيْخُ السَّنُوسِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ صُغْرَى الصُّغُرَى، وَأَشَارَ لَهُ الشَّيْخُ أَبُو العَبَّاسِ أَحْمَدُ بْنُ مُوسَى اليَمَنِيُّ ، لَكِنْ قَالَ الشَّيْخُ المَلوِيُّ : المُرَادُ أَنَّهَا تَكْفِي عَنْهُ، وَتَقُومُ مَقَامَهُ فِي مُجَرَّدِ التَّنْوِيرِ ، أَمَّا الوُصُولُ لِدَرَجَةِ الوِلَايَةِ فَلَا بُدَّ فِيهِ مِنْ شَيْخِ، كَمَا هُوَ مَعْلُومٌ عِنْدَ أَهْلِهِ ، وَاخْتَصَّتْ مِنْ بَيْنِ الأَذْكَارِ بِأَنَّهَا تُذْهِبُ حَرَارَةَ الطَّبَاعِ، بِخِلَافِ غَيْرِهَا فَإِنَّهُ يُشِيرُهَا .
There is an objection to the author because he singled out salat from salam, and it is disliked, as is its opposite; except what has come on the method of the later ones. They used as proof His saying: 'O you who believe, send blessings upon him and greet him with a greeting' where He connected them with the waw. This proof was rebutted by the fact that the waw is only for verbal conjunction, not actual conjunction, as in His saying: 'And establish prayer and give zakat.' Therefore, some adopted the method of the early ones that there is no dislike in that. Yes, it is contrary to the better course, absolutely. The hadiths on the virtue of sending blessings upon him are abundant and cannot be contained, and its specific qualities cannot be enumerated: among them is the fulfilment of needs, relief of distressing hardships, and descent of mercies. Also among them is what has been experienced of its effect in enlightening hearts, so that it is said: it suffices from the shaykh in the path and takes his place, as narrated by Sayyidi Ahmad Zarruq and al-Shaykh al-Sanusi in his commentary on al-Sughra al-Sughra, and al-Shaykh Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Musa al-Yamani pointed to it, but al-Shaykh al-Mallawi said: the meaning is that it suffices from him and takes his place in mere enlightenment; as for reaching the level of sainthood, a shaykh is necessary, as is known among its people. And it is distinguished among remembrances by removing heat of temperament, unlike others which increase it.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a critical expansion of a point in the main text where the poet said 'صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ اللهُ' without adding 'وَسَلَّمَ'. The commentator (Bajuri) first notes that this is objectionable because separating salawat from taslim is disliked, according to later scholars, who prove their position by the Quranic verse 'صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ وَسَلِّمُوا تَسْلِيمًا' where the waw indicates connection. However, this proof is rebutted by noting that the waw here is for verbal conjunction (i.e., they are mentioned together) not for actual conjunction (i.e., they must be performed together). An analogy is made with 'أَقِيمُوا الصَّلَاةَ وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ' where the actions are separate obligations. Thus, the early scholars did not consider it disliked. Nevertheless, the commentator says it is still contrary to the better practice (khilaf al-awla). Then he lists virtues of sending salawat: it fulfills needs, relieves distress, brings mercy, enlightens hearts, and can even take the place of a shaykh in spiritual enlightenment, though not in reaching sainthood. It also uniquely removes heat of temperament, unlike other remembrances that increase it.

Key Terms
الصلاة على النبي
السلام
الواو للقران الذكري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main rebuttal against the claim that the waw in Quran 33:56 requires joining salawat and taslim?
A) The waw indicates a temporal sequence.
B) The waw is for verbal conjunction only, not actual conjunction.
C) The waw is an interrogative particle.
D) The waw is redundant.

Key Takeaway
The waw in commands often indicates verbal conjunction, not necessarily that the actions must be performed together.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Given the hadith: 'The strong believer is better and more beloved to Allah than the weak believer, and in each there is good,' determine if the waw indicates that strength and weakness are both good simultaneously or separately. Justify your answer using the verbal vs. actual conjunction principle.

Parsing 'Ma Dama al-Hija' in Arabic Idiom
Al-Bajuri explains the grammatical and semantic meaning of the phrase 'ma dama al-hija'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse the grammatical construction 'ma dama' and distinguish its intended meaning of perpetuity from a literal temporal restriction.

Core Idea
'Ma dama' in Arabic idiom often implies perpetuity, not limitation.

In this passage, al-Bajuri breaks down the phrase 'ma dama al-hija' from the matn. He explains that 'ma' is a masdariyya particle with a temporal sense, but cautions that the expression is idiomatic and intends perpetuity, not a restricted duration. Understanding this requires both grammatical parsing and awareness of Arab rhetorical custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical status of 'ma'
Notice al-Bajuri calls 'ma' a masdariyya particle. This means it combines with the following verb to form a verbal noun (masdar). Here it also carries a temporal meaning (zarfiyya).
The same 'ma' can have other functions; context determines.
2
Interpret 'ma dama' as a temporal phrase
Al-Bajuri says 'ma dama' is interpreted as 'mudda' (duration). So literally it means 'for the duration of the permanence of...'.
3
Recognize the idiomatic intention of perpetuity
Al-Bajuri explicitly states that the intended meaning is not to restrict the blessing to a specific period, but to indicate perpetuity ('ta'bid'). This follows Arab custom of using such expressions hyperbolically.
This is crucial: classical Arabic often uses temporal expressions to mean 'always'.
4
Define 'al-hija'
Al-Bajuri confirms 'al-hija' (with kasr and qasr) means 'al-'aql' (intellect). This harmonizes with its usage in earlier parts of the text.
This is a lexical definition, not a logical definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (مَا دَامَ ... إلخ) «مَا مَصْدَرِيَّةٌ بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهَا آلَةٌ فِي سَبْكِ مَا بَعْدَهَا بِمَصْدَرٍ، ظَرْفِيَّةٌ، فَلِذَلِكَ فُسِّرَتْ بـ : «مُدَّةٍ» ، فَالمَعْنَى : «مُدَّةَ دَوَامَ ... إلخ»، وَلَيْسَ المُرَادُ تَقِيدَ الصَّلَاةِ بِهَذِهِ المُدَّةِ، بَلِ المُرَادُ تَابِيدُهَا ، فَكَأَنَّهُ قَالَ : صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ اللهُ دَائِماً وَأَبَداً ؛ جَرْياً عَلَى مَا هُوَ عَادَةُ العَرَبِ مِنْ ذِكْرِهِمْ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ، وَيُرِيدُونَ التَّأْبِيدَ . وَقَوْلُهُ : (الحِجَا) هُوَ - بِالكَسْرِ وَالقَصْرِ - : العَقْلُ، كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ .
His saying (ma dama ... etc.): 'ma' is a masdariyya, meaning it is a tool for casting what follows into a verbal noun, and it is zarfiyya (temporal). For that reason it is interpreted as 'mudda' (duration). So the meaning is 'for the duration of the permanence...' and the intended meaning is not to restrict the blessing to this period, but rather to indicate perpetuity. It is as if he said: May Allah bless him always and forever, following the Arab custom of mentioning such expressions and intending perpetuity. And his saying (al-hija) – with kasr and qasr – is the intellect, as has preceded.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage provides a grammatical and semantic breakdown of the matn's line. Al-Bajuri explains that 'ma' is a masdariyya (infinitive particle) combined with a temporal implication (zarfiyya), allowing it to be rendered as 'mudda' (duration). However, he clarifies that the poet does not intend to limit the blessing to a specific time, but rather uses the Arabic idiom to express perpetuity. He then defines 'al-hija' as intellect (al-'aql), confirming its meaning from earlier context.

Key Terms
ما المصدرية
الحجا

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A negative particle
C) A masdariyya particle with temporal sense
D) An interrogative particle

Key Takeaway
The particle 'ma' in 'ma dama' functions as a temporal masdar particle, and the phrase idiomatically indicates perpetuity, not temporal restriction.

Remote vs Immediate Necessary Consequences in Theological Debates
Commentator refutes extreme claims about Prophetic knowledge using logical distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the distinction between a remote necessary consequence (lāzim baʿīd) and the position itself to evaluate whether a theological claim can be attributed to an opponent.

Core Idea
A remote necessary consequence of a position is not the position itself.

In theological debates, a common tactic is to claim that an opponent's view leads to an absurd or heretical consequence. But not all consequences are entailed by the view itself. The commentator here uses the distinction between immediate and remote necessary consequences (lāzim qarīb vs. lāzim baʿīd) to defend against a charge of takfir. Understanding this logical tool is essential for fair disputation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested claim
Find the claim that the commentator is defending against the charge of takfir. It is the view that the Prophet's knowledge encompasses all things, but not in the same manner as Allah's knowledge.
2
Extract the objection against the claim
The objector (presumably al-Yusi or someone he refutes) argues that this claim would imply that the Prophet's knowledge is like Allah's, which would necessitate the temporality of Allah's knowledge (ḥudūth ʿilmihi taʿālā) because two similars share the same properties.
3
Analyze the defense using lāzim baʿīd
Al-Malawi responds that even if the claim implies such a consequence, it is a remote implication (lāzim baʿīd). The proponent of the claim does not affirm that consequence, and a remote necessary consequence is not attributable to the proponent as part of their madhhab.
The key logical principle: 'Lāzim al-madhhab laysa bi-madhhab idhā kāna lāziman baʿīdan'.
4
Assess the validity of the principle
Consider whether this principle is generally sound. It depends on the remoteness: if the consequence is logically entailed such that any rational person would recognize it, it may not be remote. The commentator implicitly distinguishes between immediate (lāzim qarīb) and remote (lāzim baʿīd) consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٧) صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ اللهُ مَا دَامَ الحِجَا يَخُوضُ مِنْ بَحْرِ المَعَانِي لُجَجَا الباجوري فَإِنَّ الخَائِضَ حَقِيقَةٌ النَّفْسُ ، وَإِنَّمَا العَقْلُ آلَةٌ كَمَا مَرَّ . قَوْلُهُ : (مِنْ بَحْرِ المَعَانِي حَالٌ مُقَدَّمَةٌ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ : «الْجَجَا»، وَمِنْ تَبْعِيضِيَّةٌ، وَالإِضَافَةُ فِي بَحْرِ المَعَانِي مِنْ إِضَافَةِ المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ لِلمُشَبَّهِ، وَالأَصْلُ: «مِنَ المَعَانِي الشَّبِيهَةِ بِالبَحْرِ فِي الكَثْرَةِ وَالسِّعَةِ». وَقَوْلُهُ : (لُجَجَا) مَفْعُولٌ بِهِ لِقَوْلِهِ : «يَخُوضُ، وَهِيَ جَمْعُ: «لُجَّةٍ»، وَهِيَ : «المَاءُ العَظِيمُ المُضْطَرِبُ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهَا هُنَا : المَسَائِلُ الصَّعْبَةُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الاسْتِعَارَةِ التَّصْرِيحِيَّةِ، فَيَكُونُ المُصَنِّفُ قَدْ شَبَّهَ المَسَائِلَ الصَّعْبَةَ بِمَعْنَى اللُّجَجِ ، وَاسْتَعَارَ لَفْظَ المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ لِلمُشَبَّهِ، وَالقَرِينَةُ : لَفْظُ المَعَانِي»، وَقَوْلُهُ : يَخُوضُ تَرْشِيحُ . لا يُقَالُ : كَيْفَ يَكُونُ كَلَامُهُ مِنْ بَابِ الاِسْتِعَارَةِ، مَعَ أَنَّ فِيهِ الجَمْعُ بَيْنَ الطَّرَفَيْنِ ؛ أَعْنِي : المُشَبَّهَ وَالمُشَبَّهَ بِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ قَدْ ذَكَرَ الأَوَّلَ فِي قَوْلِهِ : بَحْرِ المَعَانِي، وَالثَّانِي بِقَوْلِهِ : «لُجَجَا»، وَذَلِكَ مُمْتَنِعُ فيها ؟ لأَنَّا نَقُولُ : المُشَبَّهُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ خُصُوصُ المَسَائِلِ الصَّعْبَةِ، وَلَمْ يَذْكُرْهَا المُصَنِّفُ بِخُصُوصِهَا ، وَدُخُولُهَا فِي عُمُومِ المَعَانِي لا يَضُرُّ. وَفِي إِثْيَانِ المُصَنِّفِ بـ مِنْ التَّبْعِيضِيَّةِ فِي قَوْلِهِ : مِنْ بَحْرِ المَعَانِي»؛ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّهُ لَا يَحْتَوِي عَلَى جَمِيعِ المَعَانِي إِلَّا اللهُ تَعَالَى كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ فِي شَرْحِهِ» (١) ، وَهُوَ صَرِيحٌ فِي الرَّدُ(۲) عَلَى مَنِ ادَّعَى أَنَّ عِلْمَ النَّبِي له مُحِيطٌ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِحَاطَةٌ كَإِحَاطَةِ عِلْمِ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَقَدْ أَلَّفَ العَلامَةُ اليُوسِيُّ مُؤَلَّفاً فِي الرَّدْ عَلَى مَنْ زَعَمَ ذَلِكَ وَتَكْفِيرِهِ (۳) ، وَاسْتَدَلَّ عَلَى ذَلِكَ بِأَدِلَّةٍ نَقْلِيَّةٍ وَعَقْلِيَّةٍ، لَكِنِ اسْتَظْهَرَ الشَّيْخُ الأنبابي قوله: (فَإِنَّ الخَائِضَ حَقِيقَةٌ النَّفْسُ) أي : المدرك ؛ لأنَّ يخوض مستعار لـ «يدرك»؛ إذ أصلُ الخوض»: «الدخول في الماء». قوله : (حَالٌ مُقَدَّمَةٌ) أي : لأنَّه في الأصل نعت للنكرة، ونعتُ النكرة إذا تقدم عليها ينصب حالاً. : (۱) انظر : «حاشية الصبان على الشَّرح الصَّغير للملوي» (ص : (۱۲۷)، «الشرح الكبير على السُّلَّم للملوي (ص: ۱۰۷). (۲) الشرشيمي: قوله : (وَهُوَ صَرِيحٌ فِي الرَّدُّ) أي: المشار الذي هو أنَّه لا يحتوي على جميع المعاني إلَّا الله [١١/٢] صريح ... إلخ . (۳) انظر: رسائل اليوسي (٥٠٨/٢). الملوِيُّ عَدَمَ تَكْفِيرِهِ؛ لِأَنَّ اللَّوَازِمَ عَلَى مَذْهَبِهِ الَّتِي مِنْ جُمْلَتِهَا حُدُوتُ عِلْمِهِ تَعَالَى ـ لِأَنَّهُ يَجِبُ لِأَحَدٍ المِثْلَيْنِ مَا وَجَبَ لِلآخَرِ - لَا يَقُولُ بِهَا ؛ لِأَنَّ لَازِمَ المَذْهَبِ لَيْسَ بِمَذْهَبِ إِذَا كَانَ لَازِماً بَعِيداً (۱). وَالتَّحْقِيقُ الَّذِي نَعْتَقِدُهُ : أَنَّهُ لَمْ يُفَارِقِ الدُّنْيَا حَتَّى أَفَاضَ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَلَيْهِ عِلْمَ الأَشْيَاءِ كُلِّهَا ، لَكِنْ لَا تَعِلْمِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى، فَلْيُتَنَبَّه
(7) May Allah send blessings upon him as long as the mind (hija) plunges into deep waves from the sea of meanings. al-Bajuri: For the plunger is in reality the soul, and the intellect is merely a tool as previously mentioned. His statement: (min bahri al-ma'ani) is a circumstantial accusative (hal) advanced from his statement 'al-lujaja', and 'min' is partitive. The idafa in 'bahri al-ma'ani' is of the similitude, the original being 'from the meanings similar to a sea in abundance and breadth'. And his statement: (lujajan) is the object of his statement 'yakhudu', and it is the plural of 'lujjat', which is 'great tumultuous water'. The intended meaning here is 'difficult issues' via explicit metaphor (isti'ara tashrihiyya). Thus the author compared difficult issues to the meaning of lujaj, and borrowed the term of the compared-to for the compared, with the context clue being 'al-ma'ani'. And his statement 'yakhudu' is a reinforcement (tarshih). It cannot be said: How can his speech be from the category of metaphor when it combines both sides – i.e., the compared and the compared-to? For he mentioned the first in his statement 'bahri al-ma'ani' and the second in his statement 'lujajan', and that is impossible in it? Because we say: The compared is specifically the difficult issues, and the author did not mention them specifically, and their inclusion under the general 'meanings' does not harm. And the author's inclusion of the partitive 'min' in his statement 'min bahri al-ma'ani' indicates that it does not contain all meanings except Allah the Exalted, as he mentioned in his commentary (1). And it is explicit in refuting (2) those who claimed that the Prophet's knowledge encompasses everything in an encompassing like the encompassing of Allah's knowledge. Indeed, al-Allama al-Yusi authored a work refuting those who claimed that and declaring them disbelievers (3), and he supported that with transmitted and rational evidences. However, al-Shaykh al-Malawi considered it not to be takfir, because the necessary consequences of his madhhab, among which is that it would necessitate the temporality of Allah's knowledge – because it is necessary for one of the two similars what is necessary for the other – he does not affirm them; because the necessary consequence of a madhhab is not a madhhab if the necessary consequence is remote. (1) And the correct view which we hold is that he (the Prophet) did not leave this world until Allah the Exalted had bestowed upon him knowledge of all things, but not like Allah's knowledge, so one should be vigilant.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening lines of the matn, specifically the metaphorical phrase describing the Prophet's blessings. The commentator first clarifies the metaphor: 'the mind plunges into deep waves from the sea of meanings' is a complex metaphor (isti'ara tashrihiyya) where difficult issues (masa'il sa'ba) are likened to tumultuous waves (lujaj), and the act of understanding is likened to plunging (khawd). He addresses a potential objection: the line appears to combine both the compared (meanings) and the compared-to (waves) in the same sentence, which would violate the normal structure of metaphor. The response is that the compared is not explicitly 'difficult issues' but rather the general 'meanings', which includes them implicitly. The word 'min' is partitive, indicating that only some meanings are accessed, not all. This triggers a theological discussion: the partitive 'min' implies that the Prophet's knowledge does not encompass all meanings—only Allah does. The commentator then refutes those who claim the Prophet's knowledge is all-encompassing like Allah's, citing al-Yusi's work against such a view. He notes that al-Malawi did not go as far as takfir, arguing that the necessary consequences of a position are not the position itself if they are remote. The final correct view is that the Prophet was given knowledge of all things by Allah, but not in the same manner as Allah's knowledge.

Key Terms
الاستعارة التصريحية
لازم بعيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did al-Malawi not consider the extreme claim (that the Prophet's knowledge encompasses all things like Allah's) to be takfir?
A) He believed the claim was actually true.
B) He argued that the necessary consequence of the claim is remote (lāzim baʿīd) and therefore not part of the madhhab.
C) He rejected the authenticity of the transmitted evidence.
D) He thought al-Yusi was mistaken about the Prophet's knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The principle that 'a remote necessary consequence is not part of the madhhab' protects against unfair attribution of extreme implications in theological debates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the claim: 'The Quran is created.' This was a contentious position in early kalam. If someone holds this view, does it necessarily imply that the Quran is not eternal? Is that an immediate or remote consequence? Discuss using the lāzim baʿīd principle.
?
In a debate between a Hanafi and a Shafi'i on the validity of a contract, the Hanafi argues that the Shafi'i's position leads to usury (riba) because of a chain of analogies. Identify whether that consequence is immediate or remote, and whether it can be attributed to the Shafi'i as part of his madhhab.

Understanding 'Al' and Grammatical Conjunction in Praising the Prophet
The commentator explains the conjunction and defines the term 'Al' in the context of the Prophet's family.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the term 'Al' in the context of the Prophet's family and evaluate the three interpretations given by al-Bajuri.

Core Idea
The term 'Al' in Islamic piety can extend beyond blood relatives to include all believers.

In this passage, the commentator al-Bajuri explains two things: the permissibility of conjoining a noun to a genitive pronoun without repeating the preposition, and the meaning of 'Al' in the context of praising the Prophet. Understanding the scope of 'Al' is crucial for proper invocation and theological clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical issue
The commentator addresses 'عطف على الضمير المجرور'. What is the contention? Why is it relevant to the line?
The conjunction attaches to the pronoun in 'عليهم' without repeating 'على'.
2
Examine the evidence
The Quranic reading of verse 4:1 is cited. How does it support the permissibility? What is the counter-argument?
Those who forbid interpret the reading as an oath.
3
Define 'Al'
The commentator gives three interpretations: relatives, pure ones, all believers. Which does he prefer and why?
The term is a collective noun with no singular from its root.
4
Evaluate the preferred interpretation
Why does the commentator say 'all of the community of response' is preferable? What does it include that the others do not?
It includes every believer, even sinful ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸) وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ ذَوِي الهُدَى مَنْ شُبِّهُوا بِأَنْجُمِ فِي الاهْتِدَا الباجوري قَوْلُهُ : (وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ) عَظْفٌ عَلَى الضَّمِيرِ المَجْرُورِ مِنْ غَيْرِ إِعَادَةِ الجَارُ، وَهُوَ جَائِزٌ عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ عِنْدَ المُحَقِّقِينَ، وَمِنْ أَدِلَّتِهِ قِرَاءَةُ مَنْ قَرَأَ : هو تَسَاءَلُونَ بِهِ وَالْأَرْحَامِ ﴾ [النساء: ١] بِجَرِّ الأَرْحَامِ» وَمَنْ مَنَعَ ذَلِكَ يَحْمِلُ هَذِهِ القِرَاءَةَ عَلَى القَسَمِ. وَالآلُ اسْمُ جَمْعٍ لَا وَاحِدَ لَهُ مِنْ لَفْظِهِ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهِ فِي هَذَا المَقَامِ : أَقَارِبُهُ . وَقِيلَ: » (۲) «أَنْقِيَاءُ أُمَّتِهِ» (٣) . وَقِيلَ: «جَمِيعُ أُمَّةِ الإِجَابَةِ وَهُوَ الأَوْلَى؛ لِيَشْمَلَ كُلَّ مُؤْمِنٍ وَلَوْ عَاصِياً، الأنبابي قوله : (وَمِنْ أَدِلَّتِهِ) ومنها أيضاً : [من البسيط] قَدْبِنَّ تَهْجُونَا وَتَشْتِمُنَا فَاذْهَبْ فَمَا بِكَ وَالأَيَّامِ مِنْ عَجَبِ قوله : (يَحْمِلُ هَذِهِ القِرَاءَةَ عَلَى القَسَمِ) أي: والبيت على الشُّذوذ.
(8) And his family and companions, possessors of guidance, who are likened to stars in guidance. al-Bajuri: His statement: (wa alihi wa sahbihi) is a conjunction on the genitive pronoun without repeating the particle, and that is permissible according to the correct position of the verifying scholars. Among its evidences is the recitation of those who recited 'bi wa al-arham' (actually 'wa al-arham') with genitive. And whoever prohibits that interprets this recitation as oath. And 'al' is a collective noun with no singular from its own root. What is intended by it in this context is his relatives. And it was said: (2) 'the pure ones of his community' (3). And it was said: 'all of the community of response', and that is preferable, to include every believer even if sinful. al-Anbabi: His statement: (wa min adillatihi) and among them also: (in meter basit) 'qad binna tahjuna wa tashtimuna...' His statement: (yahmilu hadhihi al-qira'a 'ala al-qasam) meaning: and the line is considered anomalous.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage comments on the next line of the matn, which invokes blessings on the Prophet's family and companions. The commentator first addresses a grammatical issue: the conjunction 'wa alihi wa sahbihi' attaches to a genitive pronoun without repeating the preposition, which is permissible as attested by a Quranic variant reading of verse 4:1 (where 'wal-arham' is read in genitive). Those who forbid this interpret the reading as an oath. Then the commentator defines 'Al': it is a collective noun with no singular from its own root. In this context, it means his relatives. Two other interpretations are given: 'the pure ones of his community' and 'all of the community who respond (to the call of faith)', the latter being preferable as it includes all believers. The marginal note by al-Anbabi provides a poetic example for the grammatical rule and clarifies that the line is considered anomalous.

The definition of 'Al' is negotiated among Islamic scholars; the commentator al-Bajuri prefers an inclusive definition that covers all believers.

Understanding 'Āl' in the Blessing upon the Prophet
Bajuri explains the grammatical construction and multiple interpretations of 'Al' in the Prophet's blessing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three possible interpretations of 'Āl' in the Prophet's blessing and apply the principle of contextual clue (qarīna) to determine the intended meaning.

Core Idea
The meaning of 'Āl' depends on context; without a clue, the broadest interpretation is preferred.

In this lesson, we examine the term 'Āl' (family/kin) as used in the famous prayer for the Prophet. Like many terms in Islamic sciences, its precise referent shifts with context. Bajuri, in his commentary, clarifies the grammatical basis for the phrase and then lays out three possible meanings, showing how a contextual clue (qarīna) decides which one applies. This principle is crucial for understanding texts where precise referents matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical issue
The phrase 'wa ālihi wa ṣaḥbihi' is an apposition to the pronoun without repeating the preposition. Bajuri justifies this via the Quranic reading of 'wal-arḥām' (Sūrat al-Nisā': 1).
Grammatical point: apposition to a separated pronoun without repeating the preposition is permissible.
2
Define 'Āl' as a collective noun
'Āl' is a collective noun with no singular from its root. This affects how it can be used in Arabic.
Collective nouns often have ambiguous reference.
3
List the three interpretations
The three interpretations are: (1) his relatives, (2) the pure ones of his ummah, (3) all the responding ummah. Bajuri prefers the third to include every believer.
Note that the disagreement only arises when no contextual clue is present.
4
Understand the role of qarīna
A contextual clue (qarīna) specifies which meaning is intended. This is a key principle from usul al-fiqh applied here.
Without qarīna, the broadest meaning is preferred.
5
Apply the principle to examples
Bajuri gives three supplications with different clues, each leading to a different interpretation of 'Āl'. Match the clue to the interpretation.
Example: 'those whom You have purified' → relatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة الناظم
(۸) وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ ذَوِي الهُدَى مَنْ شُبِّهُوا بِأَنْجُمٍ فِي الاهْتِدَا
الباجوري
قَوْلُهُ : (وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ) عَظْفٌ عَلَى الضَّمِيرِ المَجْرُورِ مِنْ غَيْرِ إِعَادَةِ الجَارُ، وَهُوَ جَائِزٌ عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ عِنْدَ المُحَقِّقِينَ، وَمِنْ أَدِلَّتِهِ قِرَاءَةُ مَنْ قَرَأَ : ﴿هُوَ تَسَاءَلُونَ بِهِ وَالْأَرْحَامِ﴾ بِجَرِّ الأَرْحَامِ» وَمَنْ مَنَعَ ذَلِكَ يَحْمِلُ هَذِهِ القِرَاءَةَ عَلَى القَسَمِ.
وَالآلُ اسْمُ جَمْعٍ لَا وَاحِدَ لَهُ مِنْ لَفْظِهِ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهِ فِي هَذَا المَقَامِ : أَقَارِبُهُ . وَقِيلَ: «أَنْقِيَاءُ أُمَّتِهِ» . وَقِيلَ: «جَمِيعُ أُمَّةِ الإِجَابَةِ» وَهُوَ الأَوْلَى؛ لِيَشْمَلَ كُلَّ مُؤْمِنٍ وَلَوْ عَاصِياً،
وَهَذَا الخِلَافُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ عِنْدَ عَدَمِ القَرِينَةِ، وَإِلَّا فَمَتَى وُجِدَتِ القَرِينَةُ فُسِّرَ بِمَا يُنَاسِبُهَا ، فَهِيَ مُحَكِّمَةٌ حِينَئِذٍ :
فَإِذَا قِيلَ مَثَلاً : «اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِهِ الَّذِينَ أَذْهَبْتَ عَنْهُمُ الرِّجْسَ وَطَهَّرْتَهُمْ تَطْهِيراً» فُسِّرَ بِأَقَارِبِهِ .
- وَإِذَا قِيلَ مَثَلاً : «اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِهِ الفَائِزِينَ بِطَاعَتِكَ وَرِضَاكَ» فُسِّرَ بِأَنْقِيَاءِ أُمَّتِهِ .
- وَإِذَا قِيلَ مَثَلاً: «اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِهِ سُكَانِ جَنَّتِكَ» فُسِّرَ بِجَمِيعِ أُمَّةِ الإِجَابَةِ .
Introduction of the versifier: (8) And his family and his companions, people of guidance, who are likened to stars in guidance. al-Bajuri: His statement: (And his family and his companions) is an apposition to the accusative pronoun without repeating the preposition, and that is permissible according to the correct view of the investigators. Among the evidences for this is the recitation of one who recited: 'He is the One by whom you ask each other and the wombs' with the genitive of 'the wombs'. And whoever forbids that interprets this recitation as an oath. And 'Al' is a collective noun with no single word from its root. What is meant by it in this context is: his relatives. And it is said: 'the pure ones of his ummah'. And it is said: 'all the responding ummah'—and that is preferred, so that it includes every believer even if disobedient. And this difference of opinion only applies when there is no contextual clue; otherwise whenever a contextual clue exists, it is interpreted according to it, so that clue is decisive then. For example, if it is said: 'O Allah, send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon his family whom You have removed impurity from and purified thoroughly', it is interpreted as his relatives. And if it is said: 'O Allah, send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon his family who are successful in attaining Your obedience and pleasure', it is interpreted as the pure ones of his ummah. And if it is said: 'O Allah, send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon his family who are inhabitants of Your paradise', it is interpreted as all the responding ummah.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and grammatical explanation by Bajuri of the phrase 'wa ālihi wa ṣaḥbihi' from the matn. First, he addresses the grammatical issue: the phrase is an apposition to a separated pronoun without repeating the preposition, which is permissible, citing the Quranic reading of 'wal-arḥām' as evidence. Those who reject this construction interpret that reading as an oath. Then he defines 'Āl' as a collective noun with no singular from its root. He states that in this context it means 'his relatives', but other views exist: 'the pure ones of his ummah' and 'all the responding ummah'. He prefers the broadest meaning to include all believers, even sinners. He clarifies that the disagreement only arises when no contextual clue (qarīna) is present; if a clue exists, it determines the meaning. He provides three examples of supplications with differing clues, each leading to a different interpretation of 'Āl'. This shows the principle that contextual evidence governs the intended meaning of ambiguous terms.

Key Terms
الآل
القرينة

B) The pure ones of his ummah
C) All the responding ummah
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of Āl is governed by contextual clues; without them, the broadest meaning (all responding believers) is preferred.

Definition of 'Sahb' and Ruling on Independent Blessings
Bajuri defines 'Sahb' and rules on independent blessings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'Sahb' (الصحب) as a collective noun and state the ruling on sending independent blessings on non-prophets according to Bajuri.

Core Idea
A companion is defined by belief and meeting, not by narration; independent blessings on non-prophets are disliked.

This passage from Bajuri's commentary on al-Bannani's poem clarifies two important points: the precise definition of a companion (sahabi) and the fiqh ruling on sending blessings on non-prophets. Understanding these helps us correctly identify the people of the Prophet and practice proper etiquette in salawat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The passage defines 'Sahb' (الصحب) as a collective noun for 'Sahib' (صاحب). 'Sahib' here refers to a companion (sahabi) of the Prophet.
The collective noun form 'fa‘l' is not a plural pattern but indicates a group.
2
Extract the definition of a companion
A companion is defined as anyone who met the Prophet believing in him, physically, in the customary place, even for a moment, even if a child, and whether or not they narrated hadith.
The key conditions: meeting + belief + physical presence in the customary meeting place.
3
Test the definition's inclusivity and exclusivity
Does this definition include all recognized companions? Yes, because it includes believers who met the Prophet. Does it exclude non-companions? Yes, because it requires meeting with belief.
This definition is standard in hadith sciences.
4
Identify the ruling on independent blessings
Bajuri presents three opinions: prohibition, contrary to the better, and the verified opinion that it is makruh tanzih (disliked) because it is a practice of the people of innovation.
'Independent' means not following blessings on the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة الناظم (۸) وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ ذَوِي الهُدَى مَنْ شُبِّهُوا بِأَنْجُمٍ فِي الاهْتِدَا
الباجوري
وَالصَّحْبُ اسْمُ جَمْعِ لِـ (صَاحِبٍ) عَلَى مَا هُوَ التَّحْقِيقُ مِنْ أَنَّ صِيغَةَ «فَعْل» لَيْسَتْ مِنْ أَوْزَانِ الجُمُوعِ، وَالمُرَادُ بِـ (الصَّاحِبِ) هُنَا : الصَّحَابِيُّ وَهُوَ : مَنِ اجْتَمَعَ بِالنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مُؤْمِناً بِهِ بِبَدَنِهِ فِي مَحَلِّ التَّعَارُفِ وَلَوْ لَحْظَةٌ، وَإِنْ كَانَ غَيْرَ مُمَيِّز ; سَوَاءٌ رَوَى عَنْهُ شَيْئًا أَمْ لَا».
وَفِي كَلَامِ المُصَنِّفِ : الصَّلَاةُ عَلَى غَيْرِ الأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالمَلَائِكَةِ ، وَهِيَ مَظْلُوبَةٌ إِذَا كَانَتْ عَلَى سَبِيلِ التَّبِعِ كَمَا هُنَا، وَأَمَّا إِذَا كَانَتْ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الِاسْتِقْلَالِ :
- فَقِيلَ : بِالمَنْعِ .
- وَقِيلَ : بِأَنَّهَا خِلَافُ الأَوْلَى .
- وَالتَّحْقِيقُ : أَنَّهَا مَكْرُوهَةٌ كَرَاهَةً تَنْزِيهِ ; لِأَنَّهَا مِنْ شِعَارِ أَهْلِ البِدَعِ ، كَمَا نَصَّ عَلَيْهِ اللَّقَانِيُّ .
Introduction of the versifier: (8) And his family and his companions, people of guidance, who are likened to stars in guidance. al-Bajuri: And 'al-Sahb' is a collective noun for 'Sahib' according to the verified view that the form 'fa‘l' is not among the patterns of plurals. What is meant by 'Sahib' here is the companion (sahabi), and he is: whoever met the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, believing in him, with his body, in the customary place, even for a moment, even if he was not discerning, whether he narrated something from him or not. And in the statement of the author: sending blessings on other than prophets and angels is desired when it is as a follow-up, as here; but when it is independent: some say it is prohibited; some say it is contrary to the better; and the verified opinion is that it is disliked with a tanzih dislike, because it is a practice of the people of innovation, as al-Laqani stated.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage provides a definitional explanation of 'Sahb' (companions) and then discusses the ruling on sending blessings (salawat) on non-prophets. First, Bajuri states that 'Sahb' is a collective noun for 'Sahib', clarifying that the form 'fa‘l' is not a plural pattern—implying it is a collective noun with a singular. He defines 'Sahib' here as a sahabi: anyone who met the Prophet in belief, physically, in the customary place (i.e., during his lifetime and in the normal meeting context), even for a moment, and even if the person was a child not yet able to discern. This definition covers all who saw him, whether or not they transmitted hadith. Then, regarding the author's (al-Bajuri's own) statement about salawat: sending blessings on non-prophets and non-angels is desired when it is done as a follow-up (i.e., attached to blessings on the Prophet). But when done independently, there are three positions: prohibition, contrary to the better, and the verified opinion that it is makruh tanzih (disliked but not haram) because it resembles the practice of innovators, as cited from Al-Laqani.

Key Terms
الصحب
الصلاة على غير الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible
B) Prohibited

D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
The definition of a sahabi is inclusive yet precise, and independent blessings on non-prophets are disliked to avoid resembling innovators.

Interpreting 'Al by Contextual Evidence (Qarina)
Bajuri explains how the term 'آل' is interpreted according to accompanying context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how contextual evidence (qarina) determines the referent of the ambiguous term 'آل' in Islamic supplications and texts.

Core Idea
Context (qarina) resolves ambiguity: the same term 'آل' can refer to family, pious followers, or all believers depending on the accompanying phrase.

In Islamic texts, especially supplications, the term 'آل' (family) is ambiguous. Is it limited to the Prophet's relatives, or does it include the community? Scholars disagree in the absence of context. But as Bajuri explains, when a qualifying phrase is present, it decisively determines the meaning. This lesson unpacks that principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous term
Look for the term 'آل' in the text. Note that it can refer to different groups depending on context.
In our examples, 'آل' appears in supplications after the Prophet's name.
2
Find the accompanying qualifier
Look for a descriptive phrase that follows 'آل'. This phrase is the qarina (contextual evidence).
Examples: 'الذين أذهبت عنهم الرجس' or 'الفائزين بطاعتك'.
3
Match the qualifier to a known referent
Determine which group the qualifier points to based on Islamic teachings. For instance, 'purified from impurity' refers to Ahl al-Bayt.
The qualifier may restrict meaning to relatives, pious followers, or all believers.
4
Apply the principle
Conclude that the qarina governs interpretation. Without it, the term remains ambiguous and scholars differ.
This method is used in tafsir and fiqh to resolve lexical ambiguities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهَذَا الخِلَافُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ عِنْدَ عَدَمِ القَرِينَةِ، وَإِلَّا فَمَتَى وُجِدَتِ القَرِينَةُ فُسِّرَ بِمَا يُنَاسِبُهَا، فَهِيَ مُحَكِّمَةٌ حِينَئِذٍ : فَإِذَا قِيلَ مَثَلاً : اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِهِ الَّذِينَ أَذْهَبْتَ عَنْهُمُ الرِّجْسَ وَطَهَّرْتَهُمْ تَطْهِيراً، فُسِّرَ بِأَقَارِبِهِ . وَإِذَا قِيلَ مَثَلاً : اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِهِ الفَائِزِينَ بِطَاعَتِكَ وَرِضَاكَ فُسِّرَ بِأَنْقِيَاءِ أُمَّتِهِ - وَإِذَا قِيلَ مَثَلاً: «اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِهِ سُكَانِ جَنَّتِكَ فُسِّرَ بِجَمِيعِ أُمَّةِ الإِجَابَةِ .
This difference of opinion is only when there is no contextual evidence (qarina). Otherwise, whenever contextual evidence exists, it is interpreted according to what is appropriate for it, so it (the evidence) is decisive. For example, if one says: 'O Allah, send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon his family (آل) whom You have removed impurity from and purified thoroughly,' then it is interpreted as his relatives. And if one says: 'O Allah, send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon his family (آل) who are successful in Your obedience and pleasure,' then it is interpreted as the pure ones of his community. And if one says: 'O Allah, send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon his family (آل) who are the inhabitants of Your Paradise,' then it is interpreted as all of the responding community.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a definitional explanation by Bajuri about the term 'آل' (family) and how its meaning is determined by contextual evidence (qarina). The author states that the disagreement among scholars about the meaning of 'آل' only occurs when there is no accompanying context that clarifies it. When a contextual clue is present, it governs the interpretation. Bajuri provides three examples: (1) If the phrase includes 'those from whom You have removed impurity and purified thoroughly' (a reference to the verse of purification, 33:33), then 'آل' is interpreted specifically as the Prophet's close relatives (Ahl al-Bayt). (2) If the phrase includes 'those who are successful in Your obedience and pleasure', then 'آل' refers to the pious members of the community (the righteous followers). (3) If the phrase includes 'the inhabitants of Your Paradise', then 'آل' refers to all of the responding community (the believers who enter Paradise). Thus, the same word can have different referents depending on the context. This principle is important in understanding supplications (du'a) and theological texts.

Key Terms
القرينة
الآل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire Muslim community
B) The Prophet's relatives (Ahl al-Bayt)
C) All believers
D) The pious scholars

Key Takeaway
The meaning of the ambiguous term 'آل' is determined by the accompanying contextual evidence; without it, disagreement remains.

Defending a Simile: Analyzing the Companions-to-Stars Comparison
Author responds to an objection regarding the comparison of companions to stars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the mushabbah, mushabbah bihi, and wujah al-shabah in a simile, and construct a response to an objection that the comparison is invalid due to unequal strength.

Core Idea
A simile's validity depends on the precise aspect of similarity, not on overall superiority.

In this passage, al-Bajuri defends the poet's comparison of the Prophet's companions to stars. The objection is that companions give superior guidance (saving from eternal destruction), so the simile is flawed. Al-Bajuri replies that the comparison is only about sensory, customary guidance—stars are used for navigation, companions are followed for religious guidance. Understanding this dialectical move equips you to analyze and defend analogical arguments in Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compared and the thing compared to
Find the mushabbah (companions) and mushabbah bihi (stars) in the passage. They are the two elements of the simile.
2
Extract the explicit point of similarity (jāmi')
The poet uses the word 'ihtidā'' (being guided). Identify this as the claimed common attribute.
The commentator explains why 'ihtidā'' is chosen over 'hidāyah'.
3
Anticipate the objection
What objection could be raised? The passage states that guidance by companions is stronger (saves from eternal destruction), so the comparison might seem inappropriate.
The rule in tashbīh is that the point of similarity should be stronger in the mushabbah bihi.
4
Formulate the response by narrowing the aspect
Al-Bajuri responds by specifying that the comparison is only in sensory, customary guidance (al-ḥiss wa al-ma'lūf), not in spiritual superiority.
Narrowing the aspect preserves the rule because in sensory guidance, stars are a stronger guide.
5
Test the response's validity
Check if the response satisfies the rule: in the chosen aspect (sensory guidance), stars are indeed stronger. Thus the simile holds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : ( فِي الِاهْتِدَا) هَذَا بَيَانُ لِلجَامِعِ بَيْنَ المُشَبَّهِ وَالمُشَبَّهِ بِهِ. وَقَدْ يُقَالُ : كَانَ مُقْتَضَى الظَّاهِرِ أَنْ يَقُولَ: «فِي الهِدَايَةِ» ; لِأَنَّهَا وَصْفُ كُلِّ مِنَ المُشَبَّهِ وَالمُشَبَّهِ فَتَكُونُ هِيَ الجَامِعُ بَيْنَهُمَا ، بِخِلَافِ الاهْتِدَاءِ»، فَإِنَّهُ وَصْفٌ لِلْمُهْتَدِينَ بِكُلِّ مِنْهُمَا كَمَا لَا يَخْفَى. وَقَدْ يُجَابُ بِمَا أَشَارَ لَهُ الشَّيْخُ المَلوِيُّ مِنْ أَنَّ المُرَادَ مِنَ الِاهْتِدَاءِ كَوْنُ كُلِّ مِنْهُمَا يُهْتَدَى بِهِ، فَهُوَ مَصْدَرُ المَبْنِي لِلمَفْعُولِ ، وَلَا شَكَ أَنَّهُ صِفَةٌ لِكُلٍّ مِنْهُمَا . لَا يُقَالُ : الاهْتِدَاءُ بِالصَّحَابَةِ أَقْوَى مِنَ الاِهْتِدَاءِ بِالنُّجُومِ ; لِأَنَّ الأَوَّلَ يُنْجِي مِنَ الهَلَاكِ الأُخْرَوِيِّ، بَلْ وَمِنَ الدُّنْيَوِيِّ بِخِلَافِ الثَّانِي، فَكَيْفَ تُشَبَّهُ الصَّحَابَةُ بِالنُّجُومِ فِيهِ، مَعَ أَنَّ القَاعِدَةَ أَنَّ وَجْهَ الشَّبَه يَكُونُ أَقْوَى فِي المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ؟ لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ : التَّشْبِيهُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِاعْتِبَارِ الحِس وَالمَألُوفِ، وَلَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ الاِهْتِدَاءَ فِي المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ أَقْوَى بِهَذَا الاعْتِبَارِ، وَهَذا لَا يُنَافِي أَنَّهُ أَقْوَى فِي المُشَبَّهِ بِاعْتِبَارِ آخَرَ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ .
His statement: 'in guidance' is an explanation of the commonality between the compared and the thing compared to. It might be said: the apparent requirement was to say 'in guidance' because it is a description of each of the compared and the thing compared to, so it would be the commonality between them, unlike 'being guided', for it is a description of those who are guided by each of them, as is not hidden. And it may be answered by what al-Malawi indicated: that the meaning of 'being guided' is that each of them is used for guidance, so it is a verbal noun of the passive construction, and there is no doubt that it is a description of each of them. It should not be said: guidance by the companions is stronger than guidance by the stars, because the first saves from ultimate destruction, and even from worldly destruction, unlike the second, so how can the companions be compared to stars in this, while the rule is that the point of similarity should be stronger in the thing compared to? Because we say: the comparison is only in terms of sensory experience and what is customary, and it is not hidden that guidance in the thing compared to is stronger in this regard, and this does not contradict that it is stronger in the compared in another regard, so let it be considered.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange within the commentary on the poem's first line. The commentator first explains why the poet chose the word 'اهتداء' (being guided) instead of 'هداية' (guidance). He then anticipates an objection: since guidance by companions is spiritually superior to guidance by stars, the comparison is inappropriate. The response clarifies that the comparison is not about spiritual merit but about the sensory, customary experience of guidance—stars are visually used for navigation, so the analogy holds in that respect. The objection and answer follow a typical jadal pattern.

Key Terms
تشبيه (tashbīh): Comparison between the companions and stars based on the concept of 'being guided' (ihtidā') in a sensory sense. [Note: No significant shift; stable in Arabic rhetoric and logic.]
اهتداء (ihtidā'): The act of being guided; in this context, it is a verbal noun built for the passive meaning: 'that by which one is guided'. [Note: Here used in a technical sense to emphasize the aspect of being used for guidance rather than the attribute of guiding.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator argue that the comparison of companions to stars is valid despite the companions' superior guidance?
A) Because the companions themselves are not actually guiding.
B) Because the comparison is based on sensory, customary guidance, not spiritual merit.
C) Because the stars provide stronger guidance than the companions.
D) Because the poet made a mistake in choosing the word.

Key Takeaway
Defending a simile requires isolating a precise, shared attribute (wajh al-shabah) and showing that attribute appears more prominently in the thing compared to (mushabbah bihi) within that specific regard.
