Distinguishing Idafa Bayaniyya and Idafa Lil-Bayan
Author lists four ways to parse the genitive construction 'من أصوله قواعد'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between idafa bayaniyya and idafa li-l-bayan based on the type of generality-specificity relationship, and identify which interpretation applies in a given idafa construction.

Core Idea
The key to distinguishing idafa types lies in the pattern of generality: one-aspect vs. absolute generality-specificity.

In this passage, the commentator explores four possible ways to parse the genitive construction 'من أصوله قواعد' from the poem. Beyond the parsing, he provides the criteria to distinguish two types of idafa: بيانية and للبيان. Understanding this distinction is critical for correctly interpreting the relationship between terms in logical and grammatical texts.

Guided Path
1
List the four interpretations
Read the four paraphrases given by the commentator for the phrase 'من أصوله قواعد'. Notice how each interpretation assigns a different relationship between rules (قواعد) and principles (أصول) and the whole of logic.
These are presented as four possible parsings, not as the commentator's own preferred view.
2
Identify the condition for idafa bayaniyya
Find the criterion for idafa bayaniyya: it exists when logic is applied to both particular branches (فروع جزئية) and universal issues (مسائل كلية), creating a general-specific relationship 'from one aspect' (عموم وخصوص من وجه).
'From one aspect' means the two terms share a common matter and each has exclusive matters.
3
Identify the condition for idafa li-l-bayan
Find the criterion for idafa li-l-bayan: it exists when logic is applied only to universal issues, creating an absolute general-specific relationship (عموم وخصوص مطلق). Here, one term is always more general and the other always more specific.
In this type, they meet in one matter, but only one of them is unique in another matter.
4
Apply the criteria to the examples
Test the examples given: 'خاتم حديد' (iron ring) and 'شجر أراد' (colocynth tree). Check which type of idafa each represents based on the criteria.
Iron ring: ring and iron share the matter of being a ring, but iron is unique to material and ring is unique to form → idafa bayaniyya. Colocynth tree: tree is more general than colocynth → idafa li-l-bayan.
5
Note the scholarly disagreement
The commentator states that the distinction is the verified view (التحقيق), but some scholars say there is no difference between the two types. Be aware of this disagreement when reading other texts.
This disagreement affects how one interprets idafa constructions in classical works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَلَى الثَّانِي: «فَخُذْ قَوَاعِدَ، وَتِلْكَ الْقَوَاعِدُ بَعْضُ أُصُولٍ، وَتِلْكَ الْأُصُولُ بَعْضُهُ». وَعَلَى الثَّالِثِ: «فَخُذْ قَوَاعِدَ هِيَ أُصُولٌ، وَتِلْكَ الْأُصُولُ بَعْضُهُ». وَعَلَى الرَّابِعِ: «فَخُذْ قَوَاعِدَ، وَتِلْكَ الْقَوَاعِدُ بَعْضُ أُصُولٍ هِيَ هُوَ». وَمَحَلُّ كَوْنِ الْإِضَافَةِ فِي قَوْلِهِ: «أُصُولِهِ» بَيَانِيَّةٌ إِنْ كَانَ الْمَنْطِقُ يُطْلَقُ عَلَى الْفُرُوعِ الْجُزْئِيَّةِ كَمَا يُطْلَقُ عَلَى الْمَسَائِلِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ، حَتَّى يُوجَدَ ضَابِطُ الْإِضَافَةِ الْبَيَانِيَّةِ، وَهُوَ: أَنْ يَكُونَ بَيْنَ الْمُصَافِ وَالْمُضَافِ إِلَيْهِ عُمُومٌ وَخُصُوصٌ مِنْ وَجْهِ؛ بِحَيْثُ يَجْتَمِعَانِ فِي مَادَّةٍ، وَيَنْفَرِدُ كُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا فِي مَادَّةٍ أُخْرَى؛ كَمَا فِي قَوْلِهِمْ: «خَاتَمُ حَدِيدٍ». فَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يُطْلَقُ إِلَّا عَلَى الْمَسَائِلِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ كَانَتِ الْإِضَافَةُ لِلْبَيَانِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ وُجِدَ ضَابِطُهَا حِينَئِذٍ وَهُوَ: «أَنْ يَكُونَ بَيْنَ الْمُضَافِ وَالْمُضَافِ إِلَيْهِ عُمُومٌ وَخُصُوصٌ بِإِطْلَاقِ؛ بِحَيْثُ يَجْتَمِعَانِ فِي مَادَّةٍ، وَيَنْفَرِدُ أَحَدُهُمَا فَقَطْ فِي مَادَّةٍ أُخْرَى»؛ كَمَا فِي قَوْلِهِمْ: «شَجَرُ أَرَادٍ». وَهَذَا عَلَى مَا هُوَ التَّحْقِيقُ مِنَ التَّغَايُرِ بَيْنَ الْإِضَافَةِ الْبَيَانِيَّةِ وَالَّتِي لِلْبَيَانِ. وَقِيلَ: لَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَهُمَا.
And according to the second: 'So take rules, and those rules are some of the principles, and those principles are some of it [i.e., logic].' And according to the third: 'So take rules which are principles, and those principles are some of it.' And according to the fourth: 'So take rules, and those rules are some of the principles which are it.' And the place of the genitive construction becoming explicative in his statement 'from its principles' is if the term 'logic' is applied to the particular branches as it is applied to universal issues, so that the criterion of the explicative idafa exists, which is: that there be between the possessed and the possessor a generality and specificity from one aspect, such that they meet in one matter and each is unique in another matter; as in their statement 'iron ring'. But if it is not applied except to universal issues, then the idafa is for elucidation (للبَيَان), because its criterion is then: that there be between the possessed and the possessor an absolute generality and specificity, such that they meet in one matter and only one of them is unique in another matter; as in their statement 'tree of colocynth'. And this is according to the verification of the difference between the explicative idafa and the idafa of elucidation. And it was said: there is no difference between them.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a parsing exercise detailing four possible interpretations of the idafa in the phrase 'من أصوله قواعد'. Each interpretation gives a different relationship between rules (قواعد) and principles (أصول) and logic. The author then discusses the condition for the idafa to be explicative (بيانية) versus for elucidation (للبَيَان), based on the application of the term 'logic' to particular or universal issues. Two examples are given: 'خاتم حديد' (iron ring) and 'شجر أراد' (tree of colocynth). The commentator notes the disagreement on whether there is a distinction between the explicative idafa and the idafa of elucidation.

Key Terms
إضافة بيانية
إضافة للبيان
عموم وخصوص من وجه
عموم وخصوص مطلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Idafa bayaniyya
B) Idafa lil-bayan
C) Idafa al-tamlik
D) Idafa al-mahd

Key Takeaway
The distinction between idafa bayaniyya and idafa li-l-bayan hinges on whether the possessed and possessor have a one-aspect or absolute generality-specificity relationship; applying this distinction correctly is part of precise grammatical analysis in Islamic scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Distinguishing Rajā' from Ṭamaʿ: Hope with Means vs. Hope without Effort
Analysis of 'Wa-llāha arjū' and definition of rajā' vs. ṭamaʿ.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish rajā' from ṭamaʿ based on the criterion of taking means, and identify the logical relationship between them (inclusion vs. mutual exclusivity).

Core Idea
Rajā' is hope with effort; ṭamaʿ is hope without effort – a key distinction in Islamic ethics.

In this passage from al-Bajuri's commentary on the Sullam, we encounter not only a grammatical subtlety about the accusative case of 'Allah' but a crucial definitional distinction between two types of hope: rajā' (praiseworthy hope) and ṭamaʿ (blameworthy covetousness). Understanding this difference is essential for correctly orienting one's reliance on Allah (tawakkul) without abandoning the means. Let's unpack the logical relationship and the ethical implications.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the grammatical structure
Notice that 'Allah' is fronted and in the accusative. Bajuri says it is for glorification, not as object, despite the grammatical possibility. This teaches us that even grammar can be used to express adab.
2
Recognize the function of restriction (ḥaṣr)
By fronting 'Allah', the phrase means 'I hope only in Allah'. This is a form of emphasis that excludes other objects of hope.
3
Define rajā' and ṭamaʿ
Rajā' is defined as 'hope with taking means' (الأمل مع الأخذ في الأسباب). Ṭamaʿ is 'hope without taking means'.
4
Map the logical relationship
The text states 'كل رجاء طمع ولا عكس' – every rajā' is ṭamaʿ (in a generic sense) but not vice versa. Then it notes that sometimes ṭamaʿ is specified as hope without means, making them opposites. So there are two ranges: generic ṭamaʿ includes rajā', specific ṭamaʿ excludes rajā'.
5
Apply to ethical scenarios
Consider a farmer who plants seeds and prays for rain – that is rajā'. A person who sits idle and expects provision without work – that is blameworthy ṭamaʿ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاللَّهَ أَرْجُو أَنْ يَكُونَ خَالِصَا لِوَجْهِهِ الكَرِيمِ لَيْسَ قَالِصَا قَوْلُهُ : (وَالله أَرْجُو اللَّفْظُ الشَّرِيفُ مَنْصُوبٌ عَلَى التَّعْظِيمِ، هَكَذَا الأَدَبُ، وَلَا يُقَالُ: إِنَّهُ مَنْصُوبٌ عَلَى المَفْعُولِيَّةِ ، مَعَ أَنَّهُ الوَاقِعُ ؛ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الإِخْلَالِ بِالأَدَبِ. وَإِنَّمَا قَدَّمَهُ ؛ لإفَادَةِ الحَصْرِ ، فَكَأَنَّهُ قَالَ: وَأَرْجُو اللَّهَ لَا غَيْرَهُ . وَالرَّجَاءُ» : بِالمَدِّ كَـ : «الرَّجْوِ عَلَى وَزْنِ الضَّرْبِ، وَ: «الرَّجَاوَةِ» عَلَى وَزْنِ السَّعَادَةِ؛ مَعْنَاهُ: «الأَمَلُ مَعَ الأَخْذِ فِي الأَسْبَابِ»، بِخِلَافِ الطَّمَع ، فَإِنَّهُ الأَمَلُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مَعَ الأَخْذِ فِي الأَسْبَابِ، فَكُلُّ رَجَاءِ طَمَعٌ، وَلَا عَكْسُ، وَقَدْ يَخُصُّ الطَّمَعُ بِمَا لَمْ يَكُنْ مَعَ الأَخْذِ فِي الأَسْبَابِ، فَيَكُونُ مُبَايناً لِلرَّجَاءِ.
And Allah I hope that it be pure for His noble face, not defective. His saying 'Wa-llāha arjū': the noble word is in the accusative for glorification; such is the proper conduct, and it is not said that it is in the accusative as object, though that is the grammatical fact, because that would breach propriety. And he placed it first for the purpose of restriction, as if he said: 'I hope in Allah, not other than Him.' And 'ar-rajā'' by madd, like 'ar-rajw' on the pattern of 'ad-darb', and 'ar-rajāwa' on the pattern of 'as-sa'āda'; its meaning is 'hope with taking to the means', unlike at-ṭamaʿ (covetousness), for it is hope even if not accompanied by taking to the means. So every rajā' is ṭamaʿ, but not vice versa. And sometimes ṭamaʿ is specified for that which is without taking to the means, in which case it is contrary to rajā'.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage analyzes the second line of the Sullam. Bajuri first notes the grammatical point: 'Allah' is in the accusative for glorification (naṣb ʿalā al-taʿẓīm), not as the object of the verb, even though it grammatically could be the object. This is a matter of adab (propriety) in addressing Allah. Placing it first indicates restriction (ḥaṣr): he hopes only in Allah. Then Bajuri defines the key terms: 'rajā'' (hope) is derived from roots meaning 'to hope' and is defined as 'hope accompanied by taking the means', while 'ṭamaʿ' (covetousness) is hope without effort. Thus, every rajā' is also ṭamaʿ in the generic sense, but not vice versa. In a more restricted usage, ṭamaʿ is specified for hope without means, making it distinct and even opposite to rajā'. This precise distinction is important in Islamic ethics and theology.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Bajuri, what distinguishes 'rajā'' from 'ṭamaʿ'?
A) Rajā' is hope for worldly things, ṭamaʿ for the afterlife.
B) Rajā' is accompanied by taking means; ṭamaʿ lacks means.
C) Rajā' is stronger hope; ṭamaʿ is weaker.
D) There is no real difference; they are synonyms.

Key Takeaway
The difference between praiseworthy hope (rajā') and blameworthy covetousness (ṭamaʿ) lies in whether one takes the necessary means; they are related but not identical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Using Bajuri's definition, classify the following scenarios as rajā' or ṭamaʿ: (a) A sick person takes medicine and prays for recovery. (b) A vendor sits and expects customers without advertising. (c) A farmer irrigates and then hopes for a good harvest.
?
2. In a debate, someone argues: 'All hope is blameworthy because it is ṭamaʿ.' How would you respond using Bajuri's distinction? Provide a logical counterexample.
